### Initialize build system with autoreconf

These commands initialize the automake-based build system for individual modules within the gphoto-suite. The 'autoreconf --install --symlink' command generates necessary build files, preparing the module for configuration and compilation. This is a crucial step for projects using autotools.

```bash
alice@host:~$ (cd gphoto-suite && autoreconf --install --symlink)
```

```bash
alice@host:~$ (cd libusb && autoreconf --install --symlink)
```

```bash
alice@host:~$ (cd libexif && autoreconf --install --symlink)
```

```bash
alice@host:~$ (cd exif && autoreconf --install --symlink)
```

```bash
alice@host:~$ (cd libexif-gtk && autoreconf --install --symlink)
```

```bash
alice@host:~$ (cd libgphoto2 && autoreconf --install --symlink)
```

```bash
alice@host:~$ (cd gphoto2 && autoreconf --install --symlink)
```

```bash
alice@host:~$ (cd gphotofs && autoreconf --install --symlink)
```

```bash
alice@host:~$ (cd gtkam && autoreconf --install --symlink)
```

```APIDOC
## Configuration Options

### Description
Commands for listing, getting, and setting camera configuration parameters.

### `--list-config`

#### Description
List all configuration entries available for the camera.

#### Method
`GET` (conceptually, as it retrieves information)

#### Endpoint
`N/A (CLI Command)`

### `--list-all-config`

#### Description
List all configuration entries along with their current values and available choices.

#### Method
`GET` (conceptually)

#### Endpoint
`N/A (CLI Command)`

### `--get-config <CONFIGENTRY>`

#### Description
Retrieve the value and available options for a specific configuration entry.

#### Parameters
#### Path Parameters
* None

#### Query Parameters
* None

#### Request Body
* None

#### Example
```bash
gphoto2 --get-config capturetarget
```

### `--set-config <CONFIGENTRY>=<CONFIGVALUE>`

#### Description
Set a configuration entry to a new value. This command attempts to match the value first, then the index if a direct value match fails.

#### Parameters
#### Path Parameters
* None

#### Query Parameters
* None

#### Request Body
* None

#### Example
```bash
gphoto2 --set-config capturetarget=1
```

### `--set-config-index <CONFIGENTRY>=<CONFIGINDEX>`

#### Description
Set a configuration entry by specifying the index of the desired choice from the list of available options.

#### Parameters
#### Path Parameters
* None

#### Query Parameters
* None

#### Request Body
* None

#### Example
```bash
gphoto2 --set-config-index capturetarget=1
```

### `--set-config-value <CONFIGENTRY>=<CONFIGVALUE>`

#### Description
Set a configuration entry by directly providing its new value. This is explicit for settings with a list of choices.

#### Parameters
#### Path Parameters
* None

#### Query Parameters
* None

#### Request Body
* None

#### Example
```bash
gphoto2 --set-config-value capturetarget=Internal RAM
```
```

### Cleaning Old gphoto2 and libgphoto2 Installations

This procedure helps to resolve conflicts arising from multiple installations of gphoto2 and libgphoto2. It involves forcefully removing existing files from common installation directories before installing the newest versions.

```bash
rm -rf /usr/local/lib/gphoto2* /usr/local/lib/libgphoto2*
rm -rf /usr/lib/gphoto2* /usr/lib/libgphoto2*
```

--------------------------------

### Start Devfs Service to Apply Changes

This command activates the devfs ruleset changes made in `/etc/devfs.conf`. Running `/etc/rc.d/devfs start` applies the new permissions and ownership without requiring a system reboot. This is a necessary step after modifying the devfs configuration.

```shell
/etc/rc.d/devfs start
```

--------------------------------

### Configuring gphoto2 with PKG_CONFIG_PATH

This addresses an issue where gphoto2's configure script fails due to unmet library requirements, specifically when libgphoto2 is installed in a non-standard location. It involves setting the `PKG_CONFIG_PATH` environment variable to include the `pkgconfig` directory of the libgphoto2 installation.

```bash
PKG_CONFIG_PATH=/usr/lib/pkgconfig:/usr/local/lib/pkgconfig
export PKG_CONFIG_PATH
./configure
```

### GPContext Progress and Question Functions

Functions for starting progress tracking and asking questions to the user via the GPContext.

```APIDOC
## GPContext Progress and Questions

### `gp_context_progress_start`

#### Description
Start progress tracking. This function starts up a new progress tracking for a specified context. Several nested progress reports can happen at once, depending on the backend.

#### Method
N/A (Function Call)

#### Parameters
- **context** (*GPContext*): The context in which to start the progress.
- **target** (*float*): The 100% value.
- **_format_** (*const char*): A sprintf style string to print out, including variable arguments.
- **_..._**: Variable arguments for the format string.

#### Request Body
N/A

#### Request Example
```c
gp_context_progress_start(context, 100.0f, "Uploading file: %%d%% done", progress_percentage);
```

#### Response
Success Response:
- unsigned int: An identifier for the progress operation.

#### Response Example
```c
// Progress tracking started
```

### `gp_context_question`

#### Description
Ask frontend user a question. Asks the user a question that he must answer either with "Ok" or "Cancel". To be used by a camera driver.

#### Method
N/A (Function Call)

#### Parameters
- **context** (*GPContext*): A GPContext.
- **_format_** (*const char*): A sprintf format string.
- **_..._**: Variable arguments for format string.

#### Request Body
N/A

#### Request Example
```c
GPContextFeedback answer = gp_context_question(context, "Overwrite existing file? (Ok/Cancel)");
if (answer == GP_CONTEXT_FEEDBACK_OK) {
    // Proceed with overwrite
}
```

#### Response
Success Response:
- **GPContextFeedback**: The user's answer in form of a GPContextFeedback.

#### Response Example
```c
// Returns GP_CONTEXT_FEEDBACK_OK or other feedback codes
```
```

### Troubleshooting gphoto2 Relocation Errors with LD_LIBRARY_PATH

This section explains how to resolve 'relocation error' issues when installing new versions of gphoto2 or libgphoto2. It involves checking the currently used library files with `ldd` and setting the `LD_LIBRARY_PATH` environment variable to point to the new library installation directory.

```bash
ldd `which gphoto2`
export LD_LIBRARY_PATH=/usr/local/lib:$LD_LIBRARY_PATH
ldd `which gphoto2`
gphoto2 --version
```

### Configure Camera Settings with gphoto2

These commands allow you to interact with camera configuration settings. You can list all configuration entries, retrieve specific entry details, set entries by index or value, and start a ncurses-based configuration menu. Ensure gphoto2 is built with CDK for the menu option.

```bash
# List all configuration entries
gphoto2 --list-config

# List all configuration entries with their values and choices
gphoto2 --list-all-config

# Get a specific configuration entry
gphoto2 --get-config camera

# Set a configuration entry by value
gphoto2 --set-config " shutterspeed=1/60 "

# Set a configuration entry by index
gphoto2 --set-config-index " iso=2 "

# Set a configuration entry by value (explicit)
gphoto2 --set-config-value " focusmode=manual "

# Start the ncurses configuration menu (requires CDK build)
gphoto2 --config
```

--------------------------------

### Append and Retrieve Items from Camera Lists in C (libgphoto2)

Shows how to add (append) and retrieve (get name, get value) items from a CameraList in C using the libgphoto2 API. This is essential for populating and accessing camera configuration or detected devices. Includes functions for sorting and counting list elements.

```c
#include <gphoto2/gphoto2-list.h>
#include <stdio.h>

int main() {
    CameraList *list;
    int ret;

    gp_list_new(&list);

    // Append an item
    ret = gp_list_append(list, "camera_model", "Nikon D750");
    if (ret < 0) return ret;

    // Sort the list
    ret = gp_list_sort(list);
    if (ret < 0) return ret;

    // Get the count of items
    int count = gp_list_count(list);

    // Get name and value by index
    const char *name;
    const char *value;
    if (count > 0) {
        ret = gp_list_get_name(list, 0, &name);
        if (ret >= 0) {
            ret = gp_list_get_value(list, 0, &value);
            if (ret >= 0) {
                printf("Item 0: Name=%s, Value=%s\n", name, value);
            }
        }
    }

    gp_list_free(list);
    return 0;
}
```

### Checkout gphoto-suite from SVN

This command fetches the entire gphoto-suite source code from the SVN repository. It's the primary step for obtaining the project's codebase for compilation. Users might later comment out unwanted software in 'checkout-config.txt' and run './checkout-config.sh'.

```bash
alice@host:~$ svn _checkout_ _https://gphoto.svn.sourceforge.net/svnroot/gphoto/trunk/gphoto-suite_
```

### Get Camera Storage Information (C)

Gets information on the camera's attached storage, such as free and maximum space. The information is returned in a newly allocated array. The caller is responsible for freeing this memory. Requires a GPContext. Returns a gphoto2 error code.

```c
int gp_camera_get_storageinfo(
    Camera *camera,
    CameraStorageInformation **sifs,
    int *nrofsifs,
    GPContext *context
);
```

  "example": ""
}

#### Response Example

  "example": "{\"major\": 2, \"minor\": 5, \"patch\": 10, \"string\": \"2.5.10.1\"}"
}
```
```

# Display information about the camera's storage media
gphoto2 --storage-info

# Display the camera driver manual
gphoto2 --manual

# Display information about the camera driver

```

### Get Camera Summary Information with gphoto2 CLI

Retrieves and displays a summary of the connected camera's status, including model, owner, power status, storage information, and current time. This provides a quick overview of the camera's state.

```bash
alice@host:~$ **gphoto2 _--summary_**
Detected a 'Canon PowerShot G2'.                                                
Camera Summary:

Camera identification:
  Model: Canon PowerShot G2
  Owner: Alice Smith

Power status: on battery (power OK)

Flash disk information:
  Drive D:
   31'885'312 bytes total
   27'668'480 bytes available

Time: 2002-07-09 20:45:15 (host time +0 seconds)

alice@host:~$ 
```

### GPContext Progress Tracking Functions

Functions for starting and managing progress tracking within a GPContext.

```APIDOC
## Function Documentation

unsigned int gp_context_progress_start | ( | GPContext * | _context_ , 
---|---|---|---
| | float | _target_ ,
| | const char * | _format_ ,
| | | _..._
| )
|
Start progress tracking.
This function starts up a new progress tracking for a specified context. Several nested progress reports can happen at once, depending on the backend.

Parameters
 context| The context in which to start the progress.
 target| The 100% value.
 format| A sprintf style string to print out, including the following variable arguments.
References gp_log(), and GP_LOG_ERROR.
```

## gp_port_get_pin

### Description
Retrieves the status of a specified serial PIN (e.g., CD, CTS, DSR). The status is returned in the `_level_` parameter.

### Method
This documentation does not specify an HTTP method as it pertains to library functions, not web APIs.

### Endpoint
N/A (Library Function)

### Parameters
#### Path Parameters
N/A

#### Query Parameters
N/A

#### Request Body
N/A

### Request Example
N/A

### Response
#### Success Response (0)
Returns a gphoto2 error code. `GP_OK` (0) indicates success. The `_level_` parameter will be set to `GP_LEVEL_HIGH` or `GP_LEVEL_LOW`.

#### Response Example
```c
GPLevel level;
int result = gp_port_get_pin(port, GP_PIN_CTS, &level);
if (result == GP_OK) {
    // Check if level is GP_LEVEL_HIGH or GP_LEVEL_LOW
}
```

### Initialize and Configure Camera Object in C

Demonstrates the basic C includes and typedefs required for interacting with a Camera object in libgphoto2. This includes setting up context, configuration widgets, and capture functions. It's essential for camera initialization and interaction.

```c
#include <gphoto2/gphoto2-abilities-list.h>
#include <gphoto2/gphoto2-port.h>
#include <gphoto2/gphoto2-widget.h>
#include <gphoto2/gphoto2-filesys.h>
#include <gphoto2/gphoto2-result.h>

typedef int(* CameraPrePostFunc) (Camera *camera, GPContext *context);
typedef int(* CameraExitFunc) (Camera *camera, GPContext *context);
typedef int(* CameraGetConfigFunc) (Camera *camera, CameraWidget **widget, GPContext *context);
typedef int(* CameraGetSingleConfigFunc) (Camera *camera, const char *name, CameraWidget **widget, GPContext *context);
typedef int(* CameraListConfigFunc) (Camera *camera, CameraList *list, GPContext *context);
typedef int(* CameraSetConfigFunc) (Camera *camera, CameraWidget *widget, GPContext *context);
typedef int(* CameraSetSingleConfigFunc) (Camera *camera, const char *name, CameraWidget *widget, GPContext *context);
typedef int(* CameraCaptureFunc) (Camera *camera, CameraCaptureType type, CameraFilePath *path, GPContext *context);
typedef int(* CameraTriggerCaptureFunc) (Camera *camera, GPContext *context);
typedef int(* CameraCapturePreviewFunc) (Camera *camera, CameraFile *file, GPContext *context);
typedef int(* CameraSummaryFunc) (Camera *camera, CameraText *text, GPContext *context);
typedef int(* CameraManualFunc) (Camera *camera, CameraText *text, GPContext *context);
typedef int(* CameraAboutFunc) (Camera *camera, CameraText *text, GPContext *context);
typedef int(* CameraWaitForEvent) (Camera *camera, int timeout, CameraEventType *eventtype, void **eventdata, GPContext *context);

enum CameraCaptureType { GP_CAPTURE_IMAGE, GP_CAPTURE_MOVIE, GP_CAPTURE_SOUND };
enum CameraEventType { GP_EVENT_UNKNOWN, GP_EVENT_TIMEOUT, GP_EVENT_FILE_ADDED, GP_EVENT_FOLDER_ADDED, GP_EVENT_CAPTURE_COMPLETE };
```

### C: Initialize Camera and Set Filesystem Operations

This C code snippet demonstrates the initialization of a camera connection using libgphoto2. It involves setting various filesystem operation functions for listing, file information, file access, and folder management. It also includes port configuration and communication testing.

```c
#include "config.h"
#include <gphoto2/gphoto2-library.h>

// ... inside camera_init function ...

/* Access camera->functions directly and set them to your implementation */
camera->functions = your_camera_functions;

/* Tell the CameraFilesystem how to retrieve lists */
gp_filesystem_set_list_funcs(camera->fs, &your_list_funcs);

/* Tell the CameraFilesystem how to retrieve or set file information */
gp_filesystem_set_info_funcs(camera->fs, &your_info_funcs);

/* Tell the CameraFilesystem how to get or delete files */
gp_filesystem_set_file_funcs(camera->fs, &your_file_funcs);

/* Tell the CameraFilesystem how to put files or delete all files in a folder */
gp_filesystem_set_folder_funcs(camera->fs, &your_folder_funcs);

/* Configure the port and try to communicate with the camera */
GPResult ret;

ret = gp_port_settings_get(camera->port, &settings);
if (ret != GP_OK) return ret;

/* Adjust settings */

ret = gp_port_settings_set(camera->port, &settings);
if (ret != GP_OK) return ret;

/* Try to write to and read from the port */
if (camera_test_communication(camera) != GP_OK) {
    return GP_ERROR_COMMUNICATION;
}

return GP_OK;
```

### libgphoto2 Device Information File Structure

An example of the libgphoto2 device information file in HAL FDI format. It defines how HAL should identify and categorize USB devices supported by libgphoto2, including vendor and product IDs, and access methods.

```xml
<?xml version="1.0" encoding="ISO-8859-1"?> <!-- -*- SGML -*- -->
<!-- This file was generated by libgphoto2 print-camera-list - - fdi -->
<deviceinfo version="0.2">
 <device>
  <match key="info.bus" string="usb">
   <match key="usb.vendor_id" int="1363">
    <match key="usb.product_id" int="514">
     <merge key="info.category" type="string">camera</merge>
     <append key="info.capabilities" type="strlist">camera</append>
     <merge key="camera.access_method" type="string">proprietary</merge>
     <merge key="camera.libgphoto2.name" type="string">AEG Snap 300</merge>
     <merge key="camera.libgphoto2.support" type="bool">true</merge>
    </match>
   </match>
     ...
   <match key="usb.vendor_id" int="10096">
    <match key="usb.product_id" int="36956">
     <merge key="info.category" type="string">camera</merge>
     <append key="info.capabilities" type="strlist">camera</append>
     <merge key="camera.access_method" type="string">proprietary</merge>
     <merge key="camera.libgphoto2.name" type="string">Vivitar Vivicam35</merge>
     <merge key="camera.libgphoto2.support" type="bool">true</merge>
    </match>
   </match>
  </match>
 </device>
</deviceinfo>
```

## POST /cameras/init

### Description
Initialize a Camera object.
Sets up all the proper object function pointers, initialize camlib internal data structures, and probably establish a connection to the camera.
This is a camlib API function.

### Method
POST

### Endpoint
/cameras/init

### Parameters
#### Query Parameters
- **context** (GPContext *) - Required - Context for the operation.

### Request Body
```json
{
  "camera_config": {
    "about": true,
    "capture": true,
    "capture_preview": true,
    "exit": true,
    "get_config": true,
    "manual": true,
    "set_config": true,
    "summary": true
  }
}
```

### Response
#### Success Response (200)
- **camera** (Camera *) - The initialized camera object.

#### Response Example
{
  "camera": "<Camera object at 0x...>"
}
```

### Camera Model and Connection Settings in gphoto2

Allows specifying the camera model and serial transfer speed. Requires quoting model names with spaces and must be used with --port if --camera is specified.

```bash
# Specify the camera model (e.g., "Kodak DC240"). Requires --port.
--camera MODEL

# Specify the serial transfer speed.
--speed SPEED
```

### File Handling and Naming in gphoto2

Options for controlling how files are downloaded from or uploaded to the camera, including specifying filenames and output locations.

```bash
# Send downloaded file content to standard output.
--stdout

# Print the filesize before the file data when using --stdout.
--stdout-size

# Specify the filename or pattern for downloaded/uploaded files.
# Supports date format specifiers (e.g., %Y, %m, %d) and custom ones like %n (number).
--filename FILENAME
```

### Get File Info API

```APIDOC
## POST /websites/gphoto_doc/get_info_func

### Description
Get the file info here and write it to space provided by caller.

### Method
POST

### Endpoint
/websites/gphoto_doc/get_info_func

### Parameters
#### Path Parameters
- _fs_ (CameraFilesystem *) - Required - The camera filesystem object.
- _folder_ (const char *) - Required - The path to the folder containing the file.
- _filename_ (const char *) - Required - The name of the file to get information for.
- _info_ (CameraFileInfo *) - Required - Space provided by caller in which file info is written.
- _data_ (void *) - Optional - User data.
- _context_ (GPContext *) - Required - The gphoto2 context.

### Request Example
```json
{
  "folder": "/store_00010001/DCIM/100CANON",
  "filename": "IMG_0001.JPG",
  "info": "<allocated CameraFileInfo structure>",
  "data": null
}
```

### Response
#### Success Response (200)
- **int** - Returns GP_OK on success, or an error code.

#### Response Example
```json
{
  "example": "GP_OK"
}
```
```

### gphoto2 Client: File and Folder Operations

This snippet outlines gphoto2 commands for interacting with files and folders on the camera, including listing, creating, deleting, and downloading. It supports recursive operations and selective file retrieval.

```bash
gphoto2 [--filename FILENAME] [[-a] | [--abilities]] [[--folder FOLDER] | [-f FOLDER]] [[[-R] | [--recurse]] | [--no-recurse]] [[-l] | [--list-folders]] [[-L] | [--list-files]] [[-m NAME] | [--mkdir NAME]] [[-r NAME] | [--rmdir NAME]] [[-n] | [--num-files]]
```

### Timeout and Settings Configuration

Functions for getting and setting the port's timeout value and communication settings.

```APIDOC
## Timeout and Settings Configuration

### Description
Allows retrieval and modification of the port's timeout duration and communication parameters.

### Functions

*   **gp_port_get_timeout**
    *   **Description**: Retrieves the current timeout value for the port.
    *   **Parameters**:
        *   `GPPort *port` - The port to query.
        *   `int *timeout` - Pointer to store the timeout value.
    *   **Return Value**: `int` - 0 on success, negative on error.

*   **gp_port_set_timeout**
    *   **Description**: Sets the timeout value for the port.
    *   **Parameters**:
        *   `GPPort *port` - The port to configure.
        *   `int timeout` - The desired timeout value in microseconds.
    *   **Return Value**: `int` - 0 on success, negative on error.

*   **gp_port_set_settings**
    *   **Description**: Sets the communication settings for the port.
    *   **Parameters**:
        *   `GPPort *port` - The port to configure.
        *   `GPPortSettings settings` - The settings to apply.
    *   **Return Value**: `int` - 0 on success, negative on error.

*   **gp_port_get_settings**
    *   **Description**: Retrieves the current communication settings of the port.
    *   **Parameters**:
        *   `GPPort *port` - The port to query.
        *   `GPPortSettings *settings` - Pointer to store the retrieved settings.
    *   **Return Value**: `int` - 0 on success, negative on error.
```

### List Files on Camera Storage with gphoto2 CLI

Lists all files stored on the camera's storage medium, including their names, types, sizes, and locations. This is useful for understanding the contents before downloading.

```bash
alice@host:~$ **gphoto2 _--list-files_**
Detected a 'Canon PowerShot G2'.                                                
There are no files in folder '/'.
There are no files in folder '/DCIM'.
There are 4 files in folder '/DCIM/154CANON':
#1     CRW_5417.CRW               rd  2334 KB image/x-canon-raw
#2     IMG_5415.JPG               rd  1044 KB image/jpeg
#3     IMG_5416.JPG               rd    31 KB image/jpeg
#4     MVI_5418.AVI               rd   682 KB video/x-msvideo
There are no files in folder '/DCIM/CANONMSC'.
alice@host:~$ 
```

alice@host:~$ **gphoto2 --list-ports**
Devices found: 2
Path                             Description
--------------------------------------------------------------
serial:/dev/ttyS0                Serial Port 0                   
usb:                             Universal Serial Bus

### Camera Widget - Get ID

Retrieves the unique ID associated with a CameraWidget.

```APIDOC
## gp_widget_get_id

### Description
Retrieves the unique id of the CameraWidget.

### Method
int

### Endpoint
N/A (Function Call)

### Parameters
#### Path Parameters
None

#### Query Parameters
None

#### Request Body
- **_widget_** (CameraWidget *) - Required - The CameraWidget whose ID is to be retrieved.
- **_id_** (int *) - Output - A pointer to store the retrieved widget ID.

### Request Example
```c
// Example usage:
CameraWidget *widget;
int widget_id;
int ret = gp_widget_get_id(widget, &widget_id);
```

### Response
#### Success Response (GP_OK)
Returns GP_OK on success. The `_id_` pointer will be populated with the widget's unique ID.

#### Response Example
```c
// Success return value
int ret = GP_OK;
// widget_id now holds the unique ID of the widget.
```

ERROR HANDLING:
- Returns a gphoto2 error code.
- References GP_OK.
```

### Endpoint
/camera/storageinfo

- **num_storage_info** (integer) - The number of elements in the storage_info array.

#### Response Example

{
  "storage_info": [
    { "filesystem": "DCIM", "free_bytes": 1024, "max_bytes": 4096 },
    { "filesystem": "MISC", "free_bytes": 512, "max_bytes": 1024 }
  ],
  "num_storage_info": 2
}
```

### Debug Camera Detection Issues with gphoto2 --list-ports

This FAQ entry provides steps to troubleshoot when gphoto2 cannot detect a camera. It recommends checking camera support, running `gphoto2 --list-ports` to verify port availability (especially 'usb:' for USB devices), and ensuring `usbfs` is mounted on Linux. It also emphasizes not running gphoto2 as root and setting up hotplugging correctly.

```bash
gphoto2 --list-ports
```

```bash
gphoto2 --auto-detect
```

### gphoto2 Command-Line Client

The gphoto2 client is a versatile command-line tool for managing digital cameras. It supports a wide range of operations including listing cameras and ports, detecting cameras, setting camera configurations, capturing images and videos, and managing files on the camera.

```APIDOC
## gphoto2 Command-Line Client

### Description
The `gphoto2` command-line client provides a powerful interface to interact with digital cameras. It allows users to perform various operations such as detecting cameras, listing available options, capturing images or videos, downloading files, and managing camera settings.

### Usage
`gphoto2` [OPTIONS] [COMMAND]

### Options Overview

*   **Debugging Options:**
    *   `--debug`: Enable debug output.
    *   `--debug-logfile FILENAME`: Specify a file for debug output.
    *   `--debug-loglevel LEVEL`: Set the level of debug logging.
*   **General Options:**
    *   `-q`, `--quiet`: Suppress normal output.
    *   `-v`, `--verbose`: Enable verbose output.
    *   `-h`, `--help`: Display help message.
    *   `--usage`: Show brief usage information.
    *   `--hook-script FILENAME`: Execute a script on specific events.
*   **Camera and Port Detection:**
    *   `--list-cameras`: List available camera models.
    *   `--list-ports`: List available camera ports.
    *   `--auto-detect`: Automatically detect connected cameras.
    *   `--port PATH`: Specify the camera port to use.
    *   `--speed SPEED`: Set the USB transfer speed.
    *   `--camera MODEL`: Specify the camera model.
    *   `--usbid USBIDS`: Specify the USB ID of the camera.
*   **File Management:**
    *   `--filename FILENAME`: Set the filename template for downloads.
    *   `--folder FOLDER` or `-f FOLDER`: Specify the current folder on the camera.
    *   `--list-folders` or `-l`: List folders in the current directory.
    *   `--list-files` or `-L`: List files in the current directory.
    *   `--mkdir NAME`: Create a new directory.
    *   `--rmdir NAME`: Remove a directory.
    *   `--num-files`: Count files in the current directory.
    *   `--get-file RANGE or NAME` or `-p RANGE or NAME`: Download a file.
    *   `--get-all-files` or `-P`: Download all files.
    *   `--get-thumbnail RANGE or NAME` or `-t RANGE or NAME`: Download a thumbnail.
    *   `--get-all-thumbnails` or `-T`: Download all thumbnails.
    *   `--get-raw-data RANGE or NAME`: Download raw image data.
    *   `--get-all-raw-data`: Download all raw image data.
    *   `--get-audio-data RANGE or NAME`: Download audio data.
    *   `--get-all-audio-data`: Download all audio data.
    *   `--get-meta-data RANGE or NAME`: Download metadata.
    *   `--get-all-meta-data`: Download all metadata.
    *   `--upload-meta-data FILENAME`: Upload metadata.
    *   `--force-overwrite`: Overwrite existing files.
    *   `--new`: Use a new filename for downloads.
    *   `--delete-file RANGE or NAME` or `-d RANGE or NAME`: Delete a file.
    *   `--delete-all-files` or `-D`: Delete all files.
    *   `--upload-file FILENAME` or `-u FILENAME`: Upload a file.
*   **Configuration Options:**
    *   `--config`: Show configuration settings.
    *   `--list-config`: List all configuration entries.
    *   `--list-all-config`: List all configuration entries with values.
    *   `--get-config CONFIGENTRY`: Get the value of a configuration entry.
    *   `--set-config CONFIGENTRY=CONFIGVALUE`: Set a configuration entry.
    *   `--set-config-index CONFIGENTRY=CONFIGINDEX`: Set a configuration entry by index.
    *   `--set-config-value CONFIGENTRY=CONFIGVALUE`: Set a configuration entry by value.
    *   `--reset`: Reset configuration to defaults.
*   **Capture Options:**
    *   `--capture-preview`: Capture a preview image.
    *   `--show-preview`: Display the captured preview image.
    *   `--frames COUNT` or `-F COUNT`: Set the number of frames to capture.
    *   `--interval SECONDS` or `-I SECONDS`: Set the capture interval.
    *   `--reset-interval`: Reset the capture interval.
    *   `--capture-image`: Capture a single image.
    *   `--trigger-capture`: Trigger capture on the camera.
    *   `--capture-movie SECONDS or COUNT`: Capture a movie.
    *   `--capture-sound`: Capture sound.
    *   `--capture-tethered SECONDS, COUNT or STRING`: Capture tethered images.
    *   `--wait-event SECONDS, COUNT or STRING`: Wait for an event.
    *   `--wait-event-and-download SECONDS, COUNT or STRING`: Wait for an event and download.
*   **Information and Utility:**
    *   `--keep`: Keep files on camera after download.
    *   `--no-keep`: Do not keep files on camera after download.
    *   `--show-info RANGE or NAME`: Display image information.
    *   `--show-exif RANGE or NAME`: Display EXIF data.
    *   `--storage-info`: Display storage information.
    *   `--summary`: Show a summary of camera operations.
    *   `--manual`: Display manual mode information.
    *   `--about`: Display about information.
    *   `--shell`: Enter interactive shell mode.

### Examples

1.  **List all available cameras:**
    ```bash
    gphoto2 --list-cameras
    ```

2.  **Download all files from the camera:**
    ```bash
    gphoto2 -P
    ```

3.  **Capture an image and save it locally:**
    ```bash
    gphoto2 --capture-image-and-download
    ```

4.  **Set camera configuration:**
    ```bash
    gphoto2 --set-config "iso=800" --set-config "shootingmode=Manual"
    ```

5.  **Enter interactive shell mode:**
    ```bash
    gphoto2 --shell
    ```
```

### List Available Camera Ports with gphoto2 CLI

Lists the available ports that gphoto2 can use to connect to a camera. This helps in identifying serial or USB ports that might be used by the camera. No specific inputs are required beyond executing the command.

```bash
alice@host:~$ **gphoto2 _--list-ports_**
Devices found: 4
Path                             Description
--------------------------------------------------------------
serial:/dev/ttyS0                Serial Port 0                   
serial:/dev/ttyS2                Serial Port 2                   
serial:/dev/ttyS3                Serial Port 3                   
usb:                             Universal Serial Bus
alice@host:~$ 
```

### Start Camera Timeout

Initiates periodic calls to a specified function to keep the camera connection alive. Useful during camera initialization for cameras that require periodic messages.

```APIDOC
## int gp_camera_start_timeout ( Camera * _camera_ , unsigned int _timeout_ , CameraTimeoutFunc _func_ )

### Description
Starts a periodic timeout mechanism for the camera. The provided function `func` will be called every `timeout` seconds to keep the camera alive, preventing it from shutting down.

### Method
int

### Endpoint
N/A (Function Call)

### Parameters
#### Path Parameters
None

#### Query Parameters
None

#### Request Body
- **_camera_** (Camera*) - Pointer to the Camera object.
- **_timeout_** (unsigned int) - The interval in seconds between calls to `func`.
- **_func_** (CameraTimeoutFunc) - The function to be called periodically.

### Request Example
```
// Example usage (conceptual):
int process_id = gp_camera_start_timeout(my_camera, 60, my_keepalive_func);
if (process_id < 0) {
    // Handle error
}
```

### Response
#### Success Response (200)
- **Return Value** (int) - The ID of the background process started, or a gphoto2 error code if an error occurred.

#### Response Example
```json
{
  "process_id": 12345
}
```
```

--------------------------------

### PTP Camera Device Information File

An example of a HAL FDI file that matches all PTP class cameras based on USB interface class, subclass, and protocol. This is often included in the system and handles PTP camera detection.

```xml
<?xml version="1.0" encoding="UTF-8"?>
<deviceinfo version="0.2">
  <device>
    <match key="info.bus" string="usb">
      <match key="usb.interface.class" int="0x06">
        <match key="usb.interface.subclass" int="0x01">
          <match key="usb.interface.protocol" int="0x01">
            <merge key="info.category" type="string">camera</merge>
	    <append key="info.capabilities" type="strlist">camera</append>
            <merge key="camera.access_method" type="string">ptp</merge>
          </match>
        </match>
      </match>
    </match>
  </device>
</deviceinfo>
```

--------------------------------

### Camera Widget - Get Child by Name

Retrieves a child CameraWidget from a parent widget using its name.

```APIDOC
## gp_widget_get_child_by_name

### Description
Retrieves the child with name `name` of the widget.

### Method
int

### Endpoint
N/A (Function Call)

### Parameters
#### Path Parameters
None

#### Query Parameters
None

#### Request Body
- **_widget_** (CameraWidget *) - Required - The parent CameraWidget.
- **_name_** (const char *) - Required - The name of the child widget to retrieve.
- **_child** (CameraWidget **) - Output - A pointer to store the retrieved child CameraWidget.

### Request Example
```c
// Example usage:
CameraWidget *parent_widget;
CameraWidget *retrieved_child;
const char *child_name = " shutterspeed";
int ret = gp_widget_get_child_by_name(parent_widget, child_name, &retrieved_child);
```

### Response
#### Success Response (GP_OK)
Returns GP_OK on success. The `_child` pointer will be populated with the child widget.

#### Response Example
```c
// Success return value
int ret = GP_OK;
// retrieved_child now points to the child widget with the specified name.
```

ERROR HANDLING:
- Returns a gphoto2 error code.
- References GP_ERROR_BAD_PARAMETERS, GP_OK, and gp_widget_get_child_by_name().
- Referenced by gp_camera_get_single_config(), gp_camera_set_single_config(), and gp_widget_get_child_by_name().
```

### Camera Widget - Get Child by Label

Retrieves a child CameraWidget from a parent widget using its label.

```APIDOC
## gp_widget_get_child_by_label

### Description
Retrieves the child with label `label` of the CameraWidget.

### Method
int

### Endpoint
N/A (Function Call)

### Parameters
#### Path Parameters
None

#### Query Parameters
None

#### Request Body
- **_widget_** (CameraWidget *) - Required - The parent CameraWidget.
- **_label_** (const char *) - Required - The label of the child widget to retrieve.
- **_child** (CameraWidget **) - Output - A pointer to store the retrieved child CameraWidget.

### Request Example
```c
// Example usage:
CameraWidget *parent_widget;
CameraWidget *retrieved_child;
const char *child_label = "Exposure";
int ret = gp_widget_get_child_by_label(parent_widget, child_label, &retrieved_child);
```

### Response
#### Success Response (GP_OK)
Returns GP_OK on success. The `_child` pointer will be populated with the child widget.

#### Response Example
```c
// Success return value

// retrieved_child now points to the child widget with the specified label.
```

ERROR HANDLING:
- Returns a gphoto2 error code.
- References GP_ERROR_BAD_PARAMETERS, GP_OK, and gp_widget_get_child_by_label().
- Referenced by gp_widget_get_child_by_label().
```

### gphoto2 Client: Camera and Port Detection

This snippet covers gphoto2 options for automatically detecting connected cameras and ports, or specifying them manually. This is crucial for establishing a connection to the target device.

```bash
gphoto2 [--hook-script FILENAME] [--list-cameras] [--list-ports] [--stdout] [--stdout-size] [--auto-detect] [--port PATH] [--speed SPEED] [--camera MODEL] [--usbid USBIDS]
```

--------------------------------

### Read File Data

The `gp_filesystem_read_file` function retrieves partial file data from the filesystem starting at a specified offset.

```APIDOC
## GET /gp/filesystem/read_file

### Description
Downloads partial file data from the specified `folder` and `filename`, starting at `offset`.

### Method
GET

### Endpoint
/gp/filesystem/read_file

### Parameters
#### Path Parameters
None

#### Query Parameters
None

#### Request Body
- **fs** (CameraFilesystem *) - A pointer to the CameraFilesystem structure.
- **folder** (const char *) - The folder in which the file can be found.
- **filename** (const char *) - The name of the file to download.
- **type** (CameraFileType) - The type of the file.
- **offset** (uint64_t) - The offset where the data reading should start.
- **buf** (char *) - The target buffer where the data will be put.
- **size** (uint64_t *) - Pointer to the size to read and that was read into the buffer.
- **context** (GPContext *) - A pointer to the GPContext for the operation.

### Request Example
```json
{
  "fs": "<CameraFilesystem_pointer>",
  "folder": "/store_001",
  "filename": "IMG_0005.JPG",
  "type": "GP_FILE_TYPE_NORMAL",
  "offset": 0,
  "buf": "<buffer_pointer>",
  "size": "<size_pointer>",
  "context": "<GPContext_pointer>"
}
```

### Response
#### Success Response (200)
- **return_code** (int) - A gphoto2 error code, typically GP_OK on success.
- **data** (string) - The data read from the file (base64 encoded if binary).
- **bytes_read** (uint64_t) - The number of bytes actually read into the buffer.

#### Response Example
```json
{
  "return_code": 0,
  "data": "/9j/4AAQSkZJRg...",
  "bytes_read": 1024
}
```

### Errors
- GP_ERROR_NOT_SUPPORTED: If the `read_file_func` has not been supplied.
- Other filesystem related errors may be returned.
```

--------------------------------

### List Available Ports with gphoto2

```bash
gphoto2 --list-ports
```

- **context** (GPContext) - Required - The gphoto2 context.

### Request Example

  "camera": "<camera_object>",
  "sifs": "<storage_info_pointer>",
  "nrofsifs": "<number_of_entries_pointer>",
  "context": "<gp_context_object>"

### Folder Navigation in gphoto2

Specifies the folder on the camera to operate on. This is used for actions like listing files or downloading from a specific directory.

### Camera Widget - Get Child by ID

Retrieves a child CameraWidget from a parent widget using its unique ID.

```APIDOC
## gp_widget_get_child_by_id

### Description
Retrieves the child with id `id` of the widget.

### Method
int

### Endpoint
N/A (Function Call)

### Parameters
#### Path Parameters
None

#### Query Parameters
None

#### Request Body
- **_widget_** (CameraWidget *) - Required - The parent CameraWidget.
- **_id_** (int) - Required - The unique ID of the child widget to retrieve.
- **_child** (CameraWidget **) - Output - A pointer to store the retrieved child CameraWidget.

### Request Example
```c
// Example usage:
CameraWidget *parent_widget;
CameraWidget *retrieved_child;
int child_id = 101;
int ret = gp_widget_get_child_by_id(parent_widget, child_id, &retrieved_child);
```

### Response
#### Success Response (GP_OK)
Returns GP_OK on success. The `_child` pointer will be populated with the child widget.

#### Response Example
```c
// Success return value
int ret = GP_OK;
// retrieved_child now points to the child widget with the specified ID.
```

ERROR HANDLING:
- Returns a gphoto2 error code.
- References GP_ERROR_BAD_PARAMETERS, GP_OK, and gp_widget_get_child_by_id().
- Referenced by gp_widget_get_child_by_id().
```

### C: Initialize and Free GPPortInfoList

Demonstrates the creation and deallocation of a GPPortInfoList structure. This is essential for managing camera port information within the libgphoto2 library. It ensures proper memory management for port-related data.

```c
#include <gphoto2/gphoto2-port-info-list.h>

int main() {
    GPPortInfoList *list;
    int ret;

    // Create a new GPPortInfoList
    ret = gp_port_info_list_new(&list);
    if (ret < 0) {
        // Handle error
        return ret;
    }

    // ... use the list ...

    // Free the GPPortInfoList
    ret = gp_port_info_list_free(list);
    if (ret < 0) {
        // Handle error
        return ret;
    }

    return 0;
}
```

### Get File Index by Name

The `gp_filesystem_number` function retrieves the index of a file given its name within a specified folder.

```APIDOC
## GET /gp/filesystem/number

### Description
Looks for a file named `filename` in the given `folder` and returns its index.

### Method
GET

### Endpoint
/gp/filesystem/number

### Parameters
#### Path Parameters
None

#### Query Parameters
None

#### Request Body
- **fs** (CameraFilesystem *) - A pointer to the CameraFilesystem structure.
- **folder** (const char *) - The folder where to look for the file.
- **filename** (const char *) - The name of the file to look for.
- **context** (GPContext *) - A pointer to the GPContext for the operation.

### Request Example
```json
{
  "fs": "<CameraFilesystem_pointer>",
  "folder": "/store_001",
  "filename": "IMG_0005.JPG",
  "context": "<GPContext_pointer>"
}
```

### Response
#### Success Response (200)
- **return_code** (int) - A gphoto2 error code, typically GP_OK on success.
- **filenumber** (int) - The index of the found file.

#### Response Example
```json
{
  "return_code": 0,
  "filenumber": 5
}
```

### Errors
- GP_ERROR_DIRECTORY_NOT_FOUND: If the specified folder does not exist.
- GP_ERROR_FILE_NOT_FOUND: If the file with the given name is not found in the folder.
```

### Handle USB device addition with libgphoto2

This shell script is an example udev rule script that runs when a USB device is added. It checks if the device exists, sets ownership and permissions, determines the bus and device numbers, and then uses gphoto2 to download all files from the camera. It assumes the 'photoripper' user exists and has necessary permissions.

```shell
#!/bin/sh

test "x$ACTION" != "xadd" || exit 0
test "x$SUBSYSTEM" != "xusb_device" || exit 0

if test -e "$DEVNAME"
then
  user="photoripper"
  chown "$user" "$DEVNAME"
  chmod 0600 "$DEVNAME"

  # SUBSYSTEM == "usb_device" implies that DEVNAME == "/dev/bus/usb/123/456"
  # Determine device ID and bus ID.
  dev="$(basename "$DEVNAME")"
  bus="$(basename "$(dirname "$DEVNAME")")"

  # Download all files from that camera to incoming directory with
  # lowercase filenames
  command="/usr/bin/gphoto2 --port usb:${bus},${dev} --get-all-files"
  command="$command --filename /var/local/photodump/incoming/%:"
  echo "Executing command: $command"
  su "$photoripper" -c "$command"
else
  echo "photoripper: Given device named $DEVNAME not found."
  exit 1
fi

```

### C - Port Initialization and Management

Functions for creating, opening, freeing, and configuring GPhoto2 ports. `gp_port_new` creates a new port structure, `gp_port_open` initializes a port for use, `gp_port_free` releases resources, and `gp_port_set_info` configures port-specific details.

```c
int gp_port_new(GPPort **port);
int gp_port_open(GPPort *port);
int gp_port_free(GPPort *port);
int gp_port_set_info(GPPort *port, GPPortInfo info);
```

### Camera Pre-Operation Check Macro (C)

The CHECK_OPEN macro is designed to be executed before camera operations. It checks if a pre-function is defined and executes it, returning any error encountered. This ensures necessary setup is performed before proceeding.

```C
#define CHECK_OPEN | ( |  | c,   
---|---|---|---  
|  |  | ctx   
| ) | |   
**Value:**
{ 
if ((c)->functions->pre_func) { 
int r2 = (c)->functions->pre_func (c,ctx); 
if (r2 < 0) { 
CAMERA_UNUSED (c,ctx); 
return (r2); 
}
}
}
```

### C: Get File Information from Camera

The `get_info_func` function retrieves metadata for a specific file on the camera and stores it in the provided `CameraFileInfo` structure. This CameraFilesystem method requires the filesystem pointer, folder path, filename, a pointer to `CameraFileInfo`, user data, and a `GPContext`. It references `GP_OK` and `set_info_func()`.

```c
int get_info_func(
    CameraFilesystem * _fs,
    const char * _folder,
    const char * _filename,
    CameraFileInfo * _info,
    void * _data,
    GPContext * _context
);
```

### Camera Abilities API

Provides functions to retrieve a list of abilities for all supported cameras and initialize camera connections.

```APIDOC
## GET /camera/abilities

### Description
Retrieves a list of abilities for all supported cameras by the libgphoto2 library.

### Method
GET

### Endpoint
/camera/abilities

### Parameters
#### Query Parameters
- **list** (CameraAbilitiesList) - Required - A structure to be populated with the abilities of supported camera models.

### Request Example
```json
{
  "message": "This is a GET request, no request body needed."
}
```

### Response
#### Success Response (200)
- **status** (integer) - A gphoto2 error code indicating success or failure.
- **abilities** (array) - A list of camera abilities, where each ability is an object.
  - **model** (string) - The model name of the camera.
  - **capabilities** (array) - A list of capabilities supported by the camera.

#### Response Example
```json
{
  "status": 0, 
  "abilities": [
    {
      "model": "Nikon D750",
      "capabilities": ["capture", "download", "list_files"]
    },
    {
      "model": "Canon EOS 5D Mark IV",
      "capabilities": ["capture", "download", "delete_file"]
    }
  ]
}
```
```

### Endpoint

  - **port** (Port) - The port through which the camera is connected.
  - **fs** (Filesystem) - The filesystem object for interacting with the camera's storage.
  - **functions** (CameraFunctions) - A structure containing function pointers for camera operations.

### Request Example

  "camera": {
    "context": {"log_level": 4},
    "port": null, 
    "fs": null,
    "functions": {}
  }
}

### C: Get Camera Abilities List

This C function retrieves a list of abilities for all supported cameras by the libgphoto2 library. It requires a pointer to a CameraAbilitiesList structure, which will be populated by the function.

```c
int camera_abilities(CameraAbilitiesList *list) {
    /* For each supported camera model, fill out CameraAbilities and append to list */
    /* Example: */
    CameraAbilities abilities;
    gp_abilities_list_append(list, &abilities);
    
    return GP_OK;
}
```

### Download All Files from Camera with gphoto2 CLI

Downloads all files from the camera's storage to the current directory on the host computer. This command iterates through all detected files and saves them locally.

```bash
alice@host:~$ **gphoto2 _--get-all-files_**
Detected a 'Canon PowerShot G2'.                                                
Downloading 'CRW_5417.CRW' from folder '/DCIM/154CANON'...
Saving file as CRW_5417.CRW                                                     
Downloading 'IMG_5415.JPG' from folder '/DCIM/154CANON'...
Saving file as IMG_5415.JPG                                                     
Downloading 'IMG_5416.JPG' from folder '/DCIM/154CANON'...
Saving file as IMG_5416.JPG                                                     
Downloading 'MVI_5418.AVI' from folder '/DCIM/154CANON'...
Saving file as MVI_5418.AVI                                                     
alice@host:~$ 
```

### Stream Camera Preview to Video4Linux using FFmpeg

Configures the camera feed to be used as a Video4Linux device for webcam functionality. This involves loading the `v4l2loopback` kernel module and piping the gphoto2 output through FFmpeg to the virtual video device.

```bash
sudo modprobe v4l2loopback exclusive_caps=1 card_label="GPhoto2 Webcam"
gphoto2 --stdout --capture-movie | ffmpeg -i - -vcodec rawvideo -pix_fmt yuv420p -threads 0 -f v4l2 /dev/video1
```

### CameraFilesystemFile Data Structure

```APIDOC
## _CameraFilesystemFile Data Structure

### Description
This structure represents a file within the camera's filesystem and contains information about the file, including its name, size, and associated file objects for different formats (preview, normal, raw, etc.).

### Method
N/A

### Endpoint
N/A

### Parameters
#### Path Parameters
None

#### Query Parameters
None

#### Request Body
None

### Request Example
```json
{
  "example": "No request body associated with this data structure documentation."
}
```

### Response
#### Success Response (200)
##### Data Fields:
- **name** (char *) - The name of the file.
- **info_dirty** (int) - Flag indicating if the file information is dirty.
- **info** (CameraFileInfo) - File information structure.
- **lru_prev** (struct _CameraFilesystemFile *) - Pointer to the previous file in the LRU list.
- **lru_next** (struct _CameraFilesystemFile *) - Pointer to the next file in the LRU list.
- **preview** (CameraFile *) - Pointer to the preview version of the file.
- **normal** (CameraFile *) - Pointer to the normal version of the file.
- **raw** (CameraFile *) - Pointer to the raw version of the file.
- **audio** (CameraFile *) - Pointer to the audio version of the file.
- **exif** (CameraFile *) - Pointer to the EXIF data associated with the file.
- **metadata** (CameraFile *) - Pointer to any associated metadata.
- **next** (struct _CameraFilesystemFile *) - Pointer to the next file in a list.

}

### C: Get and Set Port Name

Provides functions to retrieve and modify the name of a specific port entry. These are fundamental for identifying and managing individual camera connections. They operate on a GPPortInfo structure.

```c
#include <gphoto2/gphoto2-port-info.h>
#include <stdio.h>

int main() {
    GPPortInfo info;
    char *name;
    int ret;

    // Assume 'info' is a valid, initialized GPPortInfo structure
    // For example, obtained via gp_port_info_list_get_info()
    // ret = gp_port_info_new(&info); // If creating new

    // Set the port name
    ret = gp_port_info_set_name(info, "MyCameraPort");
    if (ret < 0) {
        // Handle error
        return ret;
    }

    // Get the port name
    ret = gp_port_info_get_name(info, &name);
    if (ret < 0) {
        // Handle error
        return ret;
    } else {
        printf("Port name: %s\n", name);
        // Note: 'name' is allocated memory, it might need freeing
        // depending on the library's specific behavior for get functions.
        // For libgphoto2, it's often necessary to free the returned string.
        // free(name);
    }

    // Cleanup if info was created with gp_port_info_new
    // gp_port_info_free(info);
    return 0;
}
```

// 'mtime' now holds the modification timestamp.

### Load USB Drivers and Mount USB Filesystem

These commands load the necessary USB drivers (e.g., usb-uhci, usb-ohci) and mount the USB device filesystem to `/proc/bus/usb`. This makes USB devices accessible to the system and is crucial for hotplug functionality. Modern distributions may handle this automatically.

```bash
host:~# modprobe usb-uhci
host:~# modprobe usb-ohci
host:~# mount -t usbfs usb /proc/bus/usb
```

### C: Get and Set Port Path

Functions to retrieve and set the system path associated with a port entry. This is crucial for the library to locate and communicate with the actual device. These operations modify or read from a GPPortInfo structure.

```c
#include <gphoto2/gphoto2-port-info.h>
#include <stdio.h>

int main() {
    GPPortInfo info;
    char *path;
    int ret;

    // Assume 'info' is a valid, initialized GPPortInfo structure

    // Set the port path
    ret = gp_port_info_set_path(info, "/dev/bus/usb/001/002");
    if (ret < 0) {
        // Handle error
        return ret;
    }

    // Get the port path
    ret = gp_port_info_get_path(info, &path);
    if (ret < 0) {
        // Handle error
        return ret;
    } else {
        printf("Port path: %s\n", path);
        // free(path); // Potentially free memory allocated by get_path
    }

    // Cleanup if info was created with gp_port_info_new
    // gp_port_info_free(info);
    return 0;
}
```

### Get Verbose Port Error Message (C)

```c
const char* gp_port_get_error (
    GPPort *  _port_
);

/*
Parameters
     port| a GPPort
Retrieves an error message from a port. If you want to make sure that you get correct error messages, you need to call gp_port_set_error with an error message of NULL each time before calling another port-related function of which you want to check the return value.

Returns
    a translated error message
*/
```

### Manage CameraFile Data (C)

Functions for setting, getting, appending, and slurping data for a CameraFile. `gp_file_set_data_and_size` sets the data and size, `gp_file_get_data_and_size` retrieves them, `gp_file_append` adds data, and `gp_file_slurp` reads data into a buffer.

```c
int gp_file_set_data_and_size(CameraFile *, char *data, unsigned long int size);
int gp_file_get_data_and_size(CameraFile *, const char **data, unsigned long int *size);
int gp_file_append(CameraFile *, const char *data, unsigned long int size);
int gp_file_slurp(CameraFile *, char *data, size_t size, size_t *readlen);
```

```

### C: Get Port Information by Index

Retrieves detailed information about a specific port in a GPPortInfoList using its index. This function populates a GPPortInfo structure with the data of the requested port. It requires the list and the index of the desired port.

```c
#include <gphoto2/gphoto2-port-info-list.h>
#include <gphoto2/gphoto2-port-info.h>

int main() {
    GPPortInfoList *list;
    GPPortInfo info;
    int ret;

    ret = gp_port_info_list_new(&list);
    if (ret < 0) return ret;

    ret = gp_port_info_list_load(list);
    if (ret < 0) {
        gp_port_info_list_free(list);
        return ret;
    }

    if (gp_port_info_list_count(list) > 0) {
        // Get info for the first port (index 0)
        ret = gp_port_info_list_get_info(list, 0, &info);
        if (ret < 0) {
            // Handle error
        } else {
            // Use the info structure...
        }
    }

    gp_port_info_list_free(list);
    return 0;
}
```

--------------------------------

### Create and Manage GPContext in C

Demonstrates the creation, reference counting, and notification functions for GPContext in C. GPContext manages user interaction callbacks like progress, errors, and messages.

```c
#include <gphoto2/gphoto2-context.h>

// Create a new context
GPContext *context = gp_context_new();

// Increment reference count
gp_context_ref(context);

// Decrement reference count
gp_context_unref(context);

// Notify idle time
gp_context_idle(context);

// Start progress tracking
unsigned int id = gp_context_progress_start(context, 100.0, "Downloading file %d%%\n");

// Update progress
gp_context_progress_update(context, id, 50.0);

// Stop progress tracking
gp_context_progress_stop(context, id);

// Report an error
gp_context_error(context, "An error occurred: %s\n", "File not found");

// Report status
gp_context_status(context, "Status message: %s\n", "Camera initialized");

// Print a message
gp_context_message(context, "User message: %s\n", "Please wait");

// Ask a question
GPContextFeedback feedback = gp_context_question(context, "Do you want to continue? (y/n)");

// Cancel operation
gp_context_cancel(context);
```

--------------------------------

Details how to get a pointer to the raw data and the size of a CameraFile. This allows direct access to the file's content, but the pointer's lifetime is tied to the CameraFile object.

```c
int gp_file_get_data_and_size(CameraFile *file, const char **data, unsigned long int *size);

### Port Creation and Management

Functions for creating, freeing, and managing port instances.

```APIDOC
## Port Creation and Management

### Description
Provides functions to create new port instances, free existing ones, and manage port information.

### Functions

*   **gp_port_new**
    *   **Description**: Creates a new port instance.
    *   **Return**: `GPPort **port` - Pointer to the newly created port.
    *   **Return Value**: `int` - 0 on success, negative on error.

*   **gp_port_free**
    *   **Description**: Frees a port instance and releases associated resources.
    *   **Parameters**: `GPPort *port` - The port to free.
    *   **Return Value**: `int` - 0 on success, negative on error.

*   **gp_port_set_info**
    *   **Description**: Sets information for a port.
    *   **Parameters**:
        *   `GPPort *port` - The port to configure.
        *   `GPPortInfo info` - The information to set.
    *   **Return Value**: `int` - 0 on success, negative on error.

*   **gp_port_get_info**
    *   **Description**: Retrieves information about a port.
    *   **Parameters**:
        *   `GPPort *port` - The port to query.
        *   `GPPortInfo *info` - Pointer to store the retrieved information.
    *   **Return Value**: `int` - 0 on success, negative on error.
```

### gphoto2: Interval Capture with Hook Script

Captures images at a specified interval and executes a hook script after each capture. Includes options for debugging and setting USB debug levels.

```shell
gphoto2 --capture-image --interval 60 --hook-script /usr/share/doc/gphoto2/test-hook.sh
# For debugging USB issues:
# USB_DEBUG=1 gphoto2 --capture-image --interval 60 --hook-script /usr/share/doc/gphoto2/test-hook.sh
```

CameraFile *file;
int retval;

// Create a new CameraFile object
retval = gp_file_new(&file);
if (retval < GP ধৈর্য) {
    fprintf(stderr, "Error creating file: %d\n", retval);
    // Handle error
}

// Increase reference count
retval = gp_file_ref(file);
// ...

// Decrease reference count
retval = gp_file_unref(file);

// Free the CameraFile object
retval = gp_file_free(file);
if (retval < GP ধৈর্য) {
    fprintf(stderr, "Error freeing file: %d\n", retval);
    // Handle error
}

### Stream Camera Preview as Webcam using FFmpeg

Streams the live preview from a camera as a webcam feed using gphoto2 and FFmpeg. The output is directed to a local HTTP server for viewing. This is useful for video conferencing.

```bash
gphoto2 --capture-movie --stdout | ffmpeg -re -i pipe:0 -listen 1 -f mjpeg http://localhost:8080/feed.jpg
```

### C: Get Port Count from GPPortInfoList

Retrieves the total number of ports currently stored within a GPPortInfoList. This is useful for iterating through the list or determining how many devices are available. It takes a pointer to the list as input.

```c
#include <gphoto2/gphoto2-port-info-list.h>

int main() {
    GPPortInfoList *list;
    int count;
    int ret;

    ret = gp_port_info_list_new(&list);
    if (ret < 0) return ret;

    ret = gp_port_info_list_load(list);
    if (ret < 0) {
        gp_port_info_list_free(list);
        return ret;
    }

    // Get the number of ports in the list
    count = gp_port_info_list_count(list);
    // Use the count...

    gp_port_info_list_free(list);
    return 0;
}
```

### Initialize and Manage Camera Lists in C (libgphoto2)

Demonstrates how to create, reference, unreference, and free a CameraList using the libgphoto2 C API. This is fundamental for managing camera-related data structures within the library. It includes error checking using the CHECK_RESULT macro.

```c
#include <gphoto2/gphoto2-list.h>
#include <gphoto2/gphoto2-result.h>

// Macro for checking function results
#define CHECK_RESULT(result) {int r = (result); if (r < 0) return (r);}

int main() {
    CameraList *list;
    int ret;

    // Create a new CameraList
    ret = gp_list_new(&list);
    CHECK_RESULT(ret);

    // Use the list...

    // Increment reference count
    ret = gp_list_ref(list);
    CHECK_RESULT(ret);

    // Decrement reference count
    ret = gp_list_unref(list);
    CHECK_RESULT(ret);

    // Free the list
    ret = gp_list_free(list);
    CHECK_RESULT(ret);

    return 0;
}
```

--------------------------------

Adds a specified number of entries to a CameraList, often with dummy names and values when real names cannot be determined. This is typically used by camera drivers for file listing. It requires the CameraList, a format string, and the count of entries to add.

```c
int gp_list_populate(CameraList *list, const char *format, int count)

### GP Camera Manual API

Retrieves the manual for a given camera, containing information about using the camera.

```APIDOC
## GET /gp_camera_get_manual

### Description
Retrieves the `manual` for given `camera`. This manual typically contains information about using the camera.

### Method
GET

### Endpoint
/gp_camera_get_manual

### Parameters
#### Path Parameters
- **camera** (Camera) - Required - The camera object.
- **manual** (CameraText *) - Required - A pointer to store the manual text.
- **context** (GPContext) - Required - The gphoto2 context.

### Request Example
```json
{
  "camera": "<camera_object>",
  "manual": "<camera_text_pointer>",
  "context": "<gp_context_object>"
}
```

### Response
#### Success Response (200)
- **return_value** (int) - A gphoto2 error code (GP_OK on success).

#### Response Example
```json
{
  "return_value": 0
}
```
```

### C: Filesystem Operation Function Pointers

This snippet defines function pointers for various filesystem operations within the libgphoto2 library. These pointers are used to implement camera-specific filesystem interactions. They cover listing files, setting and getting file information, reading and writing file data, deleting files, and retrieving storage information. These are essential for camera drivers to integrate with the libgphoto2 framework.

```c
#include <gphoto2/gphoto2-context.h>
#include <gphoto2/gphoto2-list.h>
#include <gphoto2/gphoto2-file.h>

typedef int(* CameraFilesystemListFunc) (CameraFilesystem *fs, const char *folder, CameraList *list, void *data, GPContext *context);
typedef int(* CameraFilesystemSetInfoFunc) (CameraFilesystem *fs, const char *folder, const char *filename, CameraFileInfo info, void *data, GPContext *context);
typedef int(* CameraFilesystemGetInfoFunc) (CameraFilesystem *fs, const char *folder, const char *filename, CameraFileInfo *info, void *data, GPContext *context);
typedef int(* CameraFilesystemGetFileFunc) (CameraFilesystem *fs, const char *folder, const char *filename, CameraFileType type, CameraFile *file, void *data, GPContext *context);
typedef int(* CameraFilesystemReadFileFunc) (CameraFilesystem *fs, const char *folder, const char *filename, CameraFileType type, uint64_t offset, char *buf, uint64_t *size, void *data, GPContext *context);
typedef int(* CameraFilesystemDeleteFileFunc) (CameraFilesystem *fs, const char *folder, const char *filename, void *data, GPContext *context);
typedef int(* CameraFilesystemPutFileFunc) (CameraFilesystem *fs, const char *folder, const char *filename, CameraFileType type, CameraFile *file, void *data, GPContext *context);
typedef int(* CameraFilesystemDeleteAllFunc) (CameraFilesystem *fs, const char *folder, void *data, GPContext *context);
typedef int(* CameraFilesystemDirFunc) (CameraFilesystem *fs, const char *folder, const char *name, void *data, GPContext *context);
typedef int(* CameraFilesystemStorageInfoFunc) (CameraFilesystem *fs, CameraStorageInformation **, int *nrofstorageinformations, void *data, GPContext *context);
```

### PTP/IP Protocol Overview

Provides a high-level overview of the PTP/IP protocol, including its transport layer, port, and connection types.

```APIDOC
## PTP/IP Protocol Overview

### Description
The PTP/IP protocol operates over a standard IP network using TCP/IP socket connections. It utilizes two distinct connections: a control and data connection, and an event connection.

### Transport Layer
TCP/IP Socket Connection

### Default Port
15740

### Connections
1.  **Control & Data Connection:** Initiator (computer) driven.
2.  **Event Connection:** Responder (camera) driven.
```

Configuration and definitions for adapting libgphoto2 to OS/2 operating systems. This includes specific definitions for serial port control (termios.h emulation), baud rates, and modem line control signals. It ensures compatibility with OS/2's input/output mechanisms.

```c

# define gp_system_dir_delim '\\'

# ifndef GPIO_OS2_INCLUDED
# define GPIO_OS2_INCLUDED

/*#define IOLIBS "./libgphoto2_port"*/

# define B300 0x00000007

# define B2400 0x0000000b
# define B4800 0x0000000c

# define EXTB B38400

# define CS6 0x00000010

# define CSTOPB 0x00000040
# define CREAD 0x00000080

### Manage Camera and USB Ports with gphoto2

Commands to manage camera operations and USB port states. This includes resetting USB ports if communication locks up and displaying general camera status information. The `--reset` command is useful for re-initializing communication with a camera.

```bash
# Reset the USB port for the auto-detected camera
gphoto2 --reset

# Reset a specific USB port
gphoto2 --port usb:XXX,YYY --reset

# Display a summary of the camera's status
gphoto2 --summary
```

### Canon EOS Bulb Mode Example (Shell)

This command sequence demonstrates how to capture an image in bulb mode using gphoto2. It involves setting the shutter speed to 'bulb', waiting for a specified duration, and then downloading the captured image. This is specific to Canon EOS cameras and requires manual mode on the camera.

```shell
gphoto2 --set-config shutterspeed=bulb --wait-event=10s --set-config bulb=1 --wait-event-and-download=5s

```

```shell
gphoto2 --wait-event=2s --set-config eosremoterelease=Immediate --wait-event=5s --set-config eosremoterelease=Off --wait-event-and-download=5s

```

```shell
gphoto2 --set-config shutterspeed=bulb , and run something like: gphoto2 --wait-event=2s --set-config eosremoterelease=Immediate --wait-event=5s --set-config eosremoterelease=Off --wait-event-and-download=5s

```

```shell
gphoto2 --set-config shutterspeed=bulb , and run something like: gphoto2 --wait-event=10s --set-config bulb=1 --wait-event-and-download=5s

```

### C: Get and Set Port Type

Allows for retrieval and modification of the type of a port entry. Port types define how the library should interact with the device (e.g., USB, serial). These functions work with a GPPortInfo structure and a GPPortType enumeration.

```c
#include <gphoto2/gphoto2-port-info.h>

int main() {
    GPPortInfo info;
    GPPortType type;
    int ret;

    // Assume 'info' is a valid, initialized GPPortInfo structure

    // Set the port type (example: USB port)
    type = GP_PORT_TYPE_USB;
    ret = gp_port_info_set_type(info, type);
    if (ret < 0) {
        // Handle error
        return ret;
    }

    // Get the port type
    ret = gp_port_info_get_type(info, &type);
    if (ret < 0) {
        // Handle error
        return ret;
    } else {
        // Check the type, e.g., if (type == GP_PORT_TYPE_SERIAL) { ... }
    }

    // Cleanup if info was created with gp_port_info_new
    // gp_port_info_free(info);
    return 0;
}
```

### C: Get Unique Camera ID

This C function is designed to retrieve a unique identifier for the connected camera. It takes a pointer to a CameraText structure where the unique ID string should be written.

```c
int camera_id(CameraText *id) {
    /* Choose a unique id, e.g., the driver name */
    const char *driver_name = "my_camera_driver";
    strncpy(id->text, driver_name, sizeof(id->text) - 1);
    id->text[sizeof(id->text) - 1] = '\0'; /* Ensure null termination */
    
    return GP_OK;
}
```

### Doxygen Graph Interpretation Example

This C++ code snippet demonstrates how doxygen comments are used to generate class documentation graphs. It illustrates different types of classes (documented, undocumented, templated) and inheritance relationships (public, protected, private), which are then visualized in a graph.

```cpp
1 /*! Invisible class because of truncation */
2 class Invisible { };
3
4 /*! Truncated class, inheritance relation is hidden */
5 class Truncated : public Invisible { };
6
7 /* Class not documented with doxygen comments */
8 class Undocumented { };
9
10 /*! Class that is inherited using public inheritance */
11 class PublicBase : public Truncated { };
12
13 /*! A template class */
14 template<class T> class Templ { };
15
16 /*! Class that is inherited using protected inheritance */
17 class ProtectedBase { };
18
19 /*! Class that is inherited using private inheritance */
20 class PrivateBase { };
21
22 /*! Class that is used by the Inherited class */
23 class Used { };
24
25 /*! Super class that inherits a number of other classes */
26 class Inherited : public PublicBase,
27 protected ProtectedBase,
28 private PrivateBase,
29 public Undocumented,
30 public Templ<int>
31 {
32 private:
33 Used *m_usedClass;
34 };
```

--------------------------------

### PTP/IP State Transitions

Describes the state transitions for both the command and event connections during PTP/IP communication.

```APIDOC
## PTP/IP State Transitions

### Description
The PTP/IP protocol defines specific state transitions for establishing and maintaining connections.

### Command Connection State Transitions
| Current State | Trigger | Next State |
|---|---|---|
| Initial Phase | Type 1 (Init_Command_Request) | Type 2 (Init_Command_Ack) |
| Initial Phase | Type 1 (Init_Command_Request) | Type 5 (Init_Fail) -> EXIT |
| Type 2 (Init_Command_Ack) | Various Commands | MAINLOOP |

### Event Connection State Transitions
| Current State | Trigger | Next State |
|---|---|---|
| Initial Phase | Type 3 (Init_Event_Request) | Type 4 (Init_Event_Ack) |
| Initial Phase | Type 3 (Init_Event_Request) | Type 5 (Init_Fail) -> EXIT |
| Type 4 (Init_Event_Ack) | Events | EVENTLOOP |
| Event Loop | Various Events | EVENTLOOP |
| Main Loop | Data Transfer | Data Packet Handling (Types 9, 10, 12) |
| Main Loop | Ping | Pong (Type 13) -> EVENTLOOP |
| Main Loop | Any Cmd_Response | MAINLOOP |
```

### Get libgphoto2 Port Library Version (C)

#define __GPHOTO2_PORT_VERSION_H__

typedef enum {

} GPVersionVerbosity;

#endif

typedef const char **(*GPVersionFunc)(GPVersionVerbosity verbose);

#endif

### GPhoto2 Filesystem Operations

This section covers core functions for interacting with the camera's filesystem. It includes operations for getting file information, setting file details, deleting files, and listing directory contents. These functions are essential for managing files on a connected camera.

```c
int gp_filesystem_get_file(CameraFilesystem *fs, const char *folder, const char *filename, CameraFileType type, CameraFile *file, GPContext *context);

int gp_filesystem_set_info(CameraFilesystem *fs, const char *folder, const char *filename, CameraFileInfo info, GPContext *context);

int gp_filesystem_delete_file_noop(CameraFilesystem *fs, const char *folder, const char *filename, GPContext *context);

int gp_filesystem_set_file_noop(CameraFilesystem *fs, const char *folder, const char *filename, CameraFileType type, CameraFile *file, GPContext *context);

int gp_filesystem_number(CameraFilesystem *fs, const char *folder, const char *filename, GPContext *context);

int gp_filesystem_name(CameraFilesystem *fs, const char *folder, int filenumber, const char **filename, GPContext *context);

int gp_filesystem_free(CameraFilesystem *fs);
```

--------------------------------

### gphoto2 Camera Interaction Commands

A set of common gphoto2 commands to interact with connected digital cameras. These commands allow users to list available camera ports, auto-detect cameras, retrieve camera summaries, check storage information, list files on the camera, and download all files.

```bash
alice@host:~$ gphoto2 --list-ports
alice@host:~$ gphoto2 --auto-detect
alice@host:~$ gphoto2 --summary
alice@host:~$ gphoto2 --storage-info
alice@host:~$ gphoto2 --list-files
alice@host:~$ gphoto2 --get-all-files
```

--------------------------------

### Load System Ports

Scans the system for available camera ports and loads them into a GPPortInfoList.

```APIDOC
## POST /gp_port_info_list_load

### Description
Load system ports.

### Method
POST

### Endpoint
/gp_port_info_list_load

### Parameters
#### Request Body
- **list** (GPPortInfoList *) - Required - A #GPPortInfoList structure to populate.

### Request Example
```json
{
  "list": "<GPPortInfoList_pointer>"
}
```

### Response
#### Success Response (200)
- **status** (string) - Indicates successful loading of system ports.

#### Response Example
```json
{
  "status": "success"
}
```

### Errors
- Returns a gphoto2 error code (e.g., GP_ERROR_LIBRARY, GP_OK).
```

### Read Partial File Data from gphoto2 Filesystem

Downloads a portion of a file from the camera's filesystem starting at a given offset. It requires a CameraFilesystem object, folder path, filename, file type, offset, a buffer to store data, a pointer to the size to read/read, and a GPContext. Returns a gphoto2 error code.

```c
int gp_filesystem_read_file(
    CameraFilesystem *  _fs_,
    const char *  _folder_,
    const char *  _filename_,
    CameraFileType | _type_,
    uint64_t  _offset_,
    char *  _buf_,
    uint64_t *  _size_,
    GPContext *  _context_
);
```

#include <gphoto2/gphoto2-port-version.h>

### Camera CameraInfo Functions (C)

This snippet documents functions related to retrieving camera information, specifically `set_info_func` and `storage_info_func`. These functions are typically used within the libgphoto2 library to manage camera settings and storage details. Their implementation is found in 'template.c'.

```C
/**
 * @brief Sets the camera information function.
 *
 * @param context The gphoto2 context.
 * @param func The camera info function pointer.
 * @return GP_OK on success, or an error code.
 */
int set_info_func(GPContext *context, gphoto2_camera_info_func_t func);

/**
 * @brief Retrieves storage information from the camera.
 *
 * @param context The gphoto2 context.
 * @param storage The storage information structure.
 * @return GP_OK on success, or an error code.
 */
int storage_info_func(GPContext *context, gphoto2_storageinfo_t *storage);
```

### Windows Portability Definitions for libgphoto2

Defines and macros for adapting libgphoto2 to Windows environments, including handling file operations, string comparisons, and type definitions. It uses Win32 API calls and provides workarounds for common POSIX functions. This section is excluded when compiling for WINE.

```c
#ifndef __GPHOTO2_PORT_PORTABILITY_H__
#define __GPHOTO2_PORT_PORTABILITY_H__

#ifdef _GPHOTO2_INTERNAL_CODE

#if defined(WIN32) && !defined(__WINESRC__)

/************************************************************************
* Begin Windows definitions (but not during WINE compilation)
************************************************************************/

# include <windows.h>
/* done by mingw/wine headers ... defined to struct ... tsaes*/
#undef interface
# include <sys/types.h>
# include <sys/stat.h>
# include <string.h>
# include <stdio.h>
# include <direct.h>

# ifdef IOLIBS
# undef IOLIBS
# endif
# define IOLIBS "."
# define strcasecmp _stricmp
# ifndef snprintf
# define snprintf _snprintf
# endif

#define __func__ __FUNCTION__

typedef SSIZE_T ssize_t;

/* Work-around for readdir() */
typedef struct {
HANDLE handle;
int got_first;
WIN32_FIND_DATA search;
char dir[1024];
char drive[32][2];
int drive_count;
int drive_index;
} GPPORTWINDIR;


/* Directory-oriented functions */
# define gp_system_dir GPPORTWINDIR *
# define gp_system_dirent WIN32_FIND_DATA *
# define gp_system_dir_delim '\\'

# define sleep(x) usleep((x) * 1000 * 1000)



/************************************************************************
* End WIN32 definitions
************************************************************************/

#elif defined(__SOME_OS2_MAGIC_HERE__)

/************************************************************************
* Begin OS/2 definitions
************************************************************************/

# define strcasecmp(foo,bar) stricmp(foo,bar)
# define gp_system_dir_delim '\\'

# ifndef GPIO_OS2_INCLUDED
# define GPIO_OS2_INCLUDED
# define IOLIBS getenv("IOLIBS")
/*#define IOLIBS "./libgphoto2_port"*/
# define RTLD_LAZY 0x001


# ifndef HAVE_TERMIOS_H
# define INCL_DOSDEVIOCTL /* DosDevIOCtl values */
# define IOCTL_ASYNC 0x0001
# define ASYNC_SETBAUDRATE 0x0041
/* c_cflag bit meaning */
# define CBAUD 0x0000100f
# define B0 0x00000000 /* hang up */
# define B50 0x00000001
# define B75 0x00000002
# define B110 0x00000003
# define B134 0x00000004
# define B150 0x00000005
# define B200 0x00000006
# define B300 0x00000007
# define B600 0x00000008
# define B1200 0x00000009
# define B1800 0x0000000a
# define B2400 0x0000000b
# define B4800 0x0000000c
# define B9600 0x0000000d
# define B19200 0x0000000e
# define B38400 0x0000000f
# define EXTA B19200
# define EXTB B38400
# define CSIZE 0x00000030
# define CS5 0x00000000
# define CS6 0x00000010
# define CS7 0x00000020
# define CS8 0x00000030
# define CSTOPB 0x00000040
# define CREAD 0x00000080
# define PARENB 0x00000100
# define PARODD 0x00000200
# define HUPCL 0x00000400
# define CLOCAL 0x00000800
# define CBAUDEX 0x00001000
# define B57600 0x00001001
# define B115200 0x00001002
# define B230400 0x00001003
# define B460800 0x00001004
# define B76800 0x00001005
# define B153600 0x00001006
# define B307200 0x00001007
# define B614400 0x00001008
# define B921600 0x00001009
# define B500000 0x0000100a
# define B576000 0x0000100b
# define B1000000 0x0000100c
# define B1152000 0x0000100d
# define B1500000 0x0000100e
# define B2000000 0x0000100f

# endif /* HAVE_TERMIOS_H */

# define CIBAUD 0x100f0000 /* input baud rate (not used) */
# define CMSPAR 0x40000000 /* mark or space (stick) parity */
/* #define CRTSCTS 0x80000000 */ /* flow control */

/* modem lines */
# define TIOCM_LE 0x001
# define TIOCM_DTR 0x002
# define TIOCM_RTS 0x004
# define TIOCM_ST 0x008
# define TIOCM_SR 0x010
# define TIOCM_CTS 0x020
# define TIOCM_CAR 0x040
# define TIOCM_RNG 0x080
# define TIOCM_DSR 0x100
# define TIOCM_CD TIOCM_CAR
# define TIOCM_RI TIOCM_RNG

# define TIOCMBIC 0x06C
# define TIOCMBIS 0x06B
# define TIOCMGET 0x06E

# endif /* GPIO_OS2_INCLUDED */

# endif

#endif

```

### GPhoto2 Camera Timeout Functionality

Functions for managing timeouts and asynchronous operations. Typedefs define callback functions for starting and stopping timeouts. `gp_camera_set_timeout_funcs` registers custom timeout handlers. `gp_camera_start_timeout` and `gp_camera_stop_timeout` manage the lifecycle of timeouts.

```c
typedef int (* CameraTimeoutFunc) (Camera *camera,
GPContext *context);
typedef unsigned int (* CameraTimeoutStartFunc) (Camera *camera,
unsigned int timeout,
CameraTimeoutFunc func,
void *data);
typedef void (* CameraTimeoutStopFunc) (Camera *camera,
unsigned int id, void *data);
void gp_camera_set_timeout_funcs (Camera *camera,
CameraTimeoutStartFunc start_func,
CameraTimeoutStopFunc stop_func,
void *data);
int gp_camera_start_timeout (Camera *camera, unsigned int timeout,
CameraTimeoutFunc func);
void gp_camera_stop_timeout (Camera *camera, unsigned int id);
```

--------------------------------

### Declare GPPortLibrary Functions in C

Declares the main functions required for a libgphoto2 I/O library in C. These include `gp_port_library_type` to get the port type, `gp_port_library_list` to list available ports, and `gp_port_library_operations` to retrieve the port operations structure.

```c
GPPortType gp_port_library_type (void);
int gp_port_library_list (GPPortInfoList *list);
GPPortOperations *gp_port_library_operations (void);
```

### C: Camera Abilities List Functions

Provides functions for managing a list of CameraAbilities. This includes creating, freeing, loading abilities from files or directories, resetting the list, detecting cameras based on abilities, appending new abilities, counting the number of abilities, and looking up abilities by model name or index. These functions are essential for initializing and querying camera information.

int gp_abilities_list_free (CameraAbilitiesList *list);
