int gp_abilities_list_reset (CameraAbilitiesList *list);

int gp_abilities_list_detect (CameraAbilitiesList *list,
GPPortInfoList *info_list, CameraList *l,
GPContext *context);

int gp_abilities_list_append (CameraAbilitiesList *list,
CameraAbilities abilities);

int gp_abilities_list_count (CameraAbilitiesList *list);

int gp_abilities_list_lookup_model (CameraAbilitiesList *list,
const char *model);

CameraAbilities *abilities);
```

### Hook Scripting in gphoto2

Enables the execution of a custom script at various stages of gphoto2's operation. The script receives environment variables like ACTION and ARGUMENT to determine the event and context.

```bash
# Execute a hook script for various events (init, start, download, stop).
--hook-script FILENAME

# Example hook script logic (conceptual):
# if [ "$ACTION" = "download" ]; then
#   echo "Downloaded file: $ARGUMENT"
# fi
```

### Get Filename from Directory Entry - POSIX/C

Retrieves the filename from a directory entry structure. It takes a dirent pointer as input and returns a constant character pointer to the filename. This utility function simplifies accessing filenames from readdir results.

```c
const char* gp_system_filename (gp_system_dirent de);

/* Definition: gphoto2-port-portability.c:238 */
const char* gp_system_filename(gp_system_dirent de)
{
    /* retrieve UNIX filename out of a directory entry */
    return de->d_name;
}
```

### Get Camera Unique ID (C)

Generates and returns a unique identifier string for the camera. The function should write a unique ID into the provided CameraText structure and return GP_OK. The driver name is suggested as a suitable unique ID.

```c
int camera_id(CameraText *_id) {
    // Example: Use driver name as ID
    const char *driver_name = "my_camera_driver";
    strncpy(_id->text, driver_name, sizeof(_id->text) - 1);
    _id->text[sizeof(_id->text) - 1] = '\0'; // Ensure null termination
    return GP_OK;
}
```

### JPEG Marker Finding Functions in libgphoto2

Functions to locate specific markers within a JPEG data chunk. 'gpi_jpeg_findff' searches for the start of a marker (FF), while 'gpi_jpeg_findactivemarker' looks for a specific marker type.

```c
char gpi_jpeg_findff (int *location, chunk *picture)
char gpi_jpeg_findactivemarker (char *id, int *location, chunk *picture)
```

### CameraFilesystemFuncs Initial Value Assignment

This snippet shows the initialization of the CameraFilesystemFuncs structure with specific function pointers. Non-present fields are set to NULL, indicating the available filesystem operations for a camera.

```c
CameraFilesystemFuncs fsfuncs  
---
**Initial value:**
= {
.file_list_func = file_list_func,
.folder_list_func = folder_list_func,
.get_info_func = get_info_func,
.set_info_func = set_info_func,
.get_file_func = get_file_func,
.del_file_func = delete_file_func,
.put_file_func = put_file_func,
.delete_all_func = delete_all_func,
.storage_info_func = storage_info_func
}
```

### Debugging Options for gphoto2

Controls the verbosity and output destination for debugging information. It allows enabling debug output, specifying a log file, and setting the log level.

```bash
# Turn on debugging output, written to stderr by default.
--debug

# Specify a file to write debugging information to.
--debug-logfile FILENAME

# Set the verbosity level for debug logging (error, debug, data, all).
--debug-loglevel LEVEL
```

### libgphoto2 CameraFile Structure and Functions (C)

Provides functions for creating, managing, and manipulating CameraFile objects, which represent files from a digital camera. Includes operations for setting/getting names, MIME types, modification times, data, and saving/loading files. Requires including <time.h> and <stdint.h>.

```c
struct _CameraFileHandler
struct _CameraFile

typedef struct _CameraFileHandler CameraFileHandler
typedef struct _CameraFile CameraFile

int gp_file_new (CameraFile **file)
int gp_file_new_from_fd (CameraFile **file, int fd)
int gp_file_new_from_handler (CameraFile **file, CameraFileHandler *handler, void *priv)
int gp_file_ref (CameraFile *file)
int gp_file_unref (CameraFile *file)
int gp_file_free (CameraFile *file)
int gp_file_set_name (CameraFile *file, const char *name)
int gp_file_get_name (CameraFile *file, const char **name)
int gp_file_set_mime_type (CameraFile *file, const char *mime_type)
int gp_file_get_mime_type (CameraFile *file, const char **mime_type)
int gp_file_set_mtime (CameraFile *file, time_t mtime)
int gp_file_get_mtime (CameraFile *file, time_t *mtime)
int gp_file_detect_mime_type (CameraFile *file)
int gp_file_adjust_name_for_mime_type (CameraFile *file)
int gp_file_get_name_by_type (CameraFile *file, const char *basename, CameraFileType type, char **newname)
int gp_file_set_data_and_size (CameraFile *, char *data, unsigned long int size)
int gp_file_get_data_and_size (CameraFile *, const char **data, unsigned long int *size)
int gp_file_open (CameraFile *file, const char *filename)
int gp_file_save (CameraFile *file, const char *filename)
int gp_file_clean (CameraFile *file)
int gp_file_copy (CameraFile *destination, CameraFile *source)
int gp_file_append (CameraFile *, const char *data, unsigned long int size)
int gp_file_slurp (CameraFile *, char *data, size_t size, size_t *readlen)

```

### Check if Path is Absolute (C)

This macro checks if a given path string starts with a '/'. If not, it generates an error message indicating that the path is not absolute and returns a specific error code. It relies on the `gp_context_error` function for error reporting.

```c
#define CA | ( |  | f,   
---|---|---|---  
|  |  | c   
| ) | |   
**Value:**
{ \
if ((f)[0] != '/') { \
gp_context_error ((c), \
_("The path '%s' is not absolute."), (f)); \
return (GP_ERROR_PATH_NOT_ABSOLUTE); \
} \
}
```

### Generate linux-hotplug usermap for libgphoto2

This command generates a usermap file for linux-hotplug, which is used to list device descriptions. The output is redirected to a specific usermap file in /etc/hotplug/usb/.

```bash
host:~# **/usr/lib/libgphoto2/print-camera-list usb-usermap \
    > /etc/hotplug/usb/_usbcam_.usermap**
```

### `gp_port_info_list_lookup_name`

#### Description
Looks up a port in the list by its name.

#### Method
N/A (Library Function)

#### Endpoint
N/A

#### Parameters
##### Path Parameters
None

##### Query Parameters
None

##### Request Body
- **list** (GPPortInfoList *) - The port information list to search within.
- **name** (const char *) - The name of the port to look up.

#### Returns
- An integer index if the port is found, otherwise an error code.

### `gp_port_info_list_get_info`

#### Description
Retrieves the port information for a specific entry in the list by its index.

#### Method
N/A (Library Function)

#### Endpoint
N/A

#### Parameters
##### Path Parameters
None

##### Query Parameters
None

##### Request Body
- **list** (GPPortInfoList *) - The port information list.
- **n** (int) - The index of the port information to retrieve.
- **info** (GPPortInfo *) - Output parameter to store the retrieved port information.

### Request Example
```c
GPPortInfoList *list;
GPPortInfo info;

if (gp_port_info_list_new(&list) == GP_OK) {
    if (gp_port_info_list_load(list) == GP_OK) {
        int count = gp_port_info_list_count(list);
        printf("Found %d ports.\n", count);
        if (gp_port_info_list_get_info(list, 0, &info) == GP_OK) {
            char *name;
            gp_port_info_get_name(info, &name);
            printf("First port name: %s\n", name);
        }
    }
    gp_port_info_list_free(list);
}
```

### Response Example
N/A (Library function return values indicate success or failure, typically `GP_OK` for success.)
```

```c
int camera_id(
    CameraText * _id_
);

### Detect Cameras and Populate CameraList using libgphoto2 C API

This function detects available cameras based on provided port information and populates a CameraList. It utilizes a CameraAbilitiesList to match detected devices with known camera drivers. It requires the abilities list, port info list, camera list, and a GPContext.

```c
#include <gphoto2/gphoto2-abilities-list.h>
#include <gphoto2/gphoto2-port-info-list.h>
#include <gphoto2/gphoto2-camera.h>
#include <gphoto2/gphoto2-context.h>

int gp_abilities_list_detect(CameraAbilitiesList *list, GPPortInfoList *info_list, CameraList *l, GPContext *context);
```

--------------------------------

### Get Value of CameraList Entry in C

Retrieves the value of an entry at a specific index within a CameraList. This function is complementary to gp_list_get_name and is used to fetch the associated data for an entry. It requires the CameraList pointer, the index, and a pointer to store the value.

```c
int gp_list_get_value(CameraList *list, int index, const char **value)
```

--------------------------------

### Get Camera Abilities by Index (C)

Retrieves the CameraAbilities for a specific entry in the CameraAbilitiesList using its index. This function returns a gphoto2 error code and is often followed by gp_camera_set_abilities(). It references various GP_DEVICE, GP_DRIVER_STATUS, GP_FILE_OPERATION, GP_FOLDER_OPERATION, GP_OK, and GP_OPERATION constants.

```c
int gp_abilities_list_get_abilities(
    CameraAbilitiesList *_list_,
    int _index_,
    CameraAbilities *_abilities_
);
```

### Get Verbose Port Error Message (C)

### Verify Device Permissions on FreeBSD (Older Versions)

This command lists the details of `/dev/ugen*` devices, showing their permissions, owner, group, and timestamps. On FreeBSD 7 and earlier, USB devices are typically represented under `/dev/ugen*`. The output should reflect the permissions set in `devfs.conf`.

```shell
ls -l /dev/ugen*
```

### C: GPContext Creation and Management

Provides functions for creating a new GPContext, and for managing its reference count. These are essential for proper memory management and resource handling when working with the libgphoto2 library.

```c
#ifndef __GPHOTO2_CONTEXT_H__
#define __GPHOTO2_CONTEXT_H__

#include <stdarg.h>

#ifdef __cplusplus
extern "C" {
#endif /* __cplusplus */

typedef struct _GPContext GPContext;

GPContext *gp_context_new (void);

void gp_context_ref (GPContext *context);
void gp_context_unref (GPContext *context);

#ifdef __cplusplus
}
#endif /* __cplusplus */

#endif /* __GPHOTO2_CONTEXT_H__ */
```

### Get Camera File Information (C)

Retrieves detailed information about a specific file within a camera's filesystem. It requires a CameraFilesystem object, folder path, filename, a CameraFileInfo structure to store the results, and a GPContext. It returns a gphoto2 error code indicating success or failure, with potential errors including GP_ERROR_NOT_SUPPORTED.

```c
int gp_filesystem_get_info(
    CameraFilesystem *  _fs_,
    const char *  _folder_,
    const char *  _filename_,
    CameraFileInfo *  _info_,
    GPContext *  _context_
);
```

These functions allow for the creation and destruction of widgets, reference counting, appending/prepending child widgets, and retrieving widgets by various criteria like label, ID, or name. They also include functions for setting and getting widget values, names, information, IDs, types, and labels. Range-specific functions and functions for managing choices within widgets are also provided.

int gp_widget_get_value (CameraWidget *widget, void *value);

int gp_widget_get_name (CameraWidget *widget, const char **name);

    a gphoto2 error code

### typedef int(* CameraLibraryInitFunc) (Camera *camera, GPContext *context)

Initializes the camera.

Parameters
     camera| a Camera
     context| a GPContext

Returns
    a gphoto2 error code

The camera driver will establish a first connection to the camera and configure the camera variable (i.e. using #gp_filesystem_set_list_funcs or gp_port_get_settings).
```

### Get String Representation of Port Result Code (C)

The `gp_port_result_as_string` function converts a gphoto2 error code (integer) into its corresponding string representation. This is useful for debugging and user feedback. It relies on static error descriptions.

```c
#include <gphoto2/gphoto2-port-result.h>

// ... other code ...

const char *result_string = gp_port_result_as_string(GP_OK);
// result_string will contain a human-readable description of the GP_OK status.
```

### System Directory and File Operations

Provides functions for creating, removing, opening, reading, and closing directories, as well as retrieving filenames and checking if a path is a file or directory.

```APIDOC
## System Directory and File Operations

### Description

This section details the portability functions for interacting with the file system, enabling easier porting to non-UNIX environments like Windows.

### Functions

#### `gp_system_mkdir`

*   **Description**: Creates a directory. Mirrors UNIX `mkdir` functionality.
*   **Parameters**: `dirname` (const char *) - The path of the directory to create.
*   **Returns**: An integer indicating success or failure.

#### `gp_system_rmdir`

*   **Description**: Removes a directory. Mirrors UNIX `rmdir` functionality.
*   **Parameters**: `dirname` (const char *) - The path of the directory to remove.
*   **Returns**: An integer indicating success or failure.

#### `gp_system_opendir`

*   **Description**: Opens a directory for reading. Mirrors UNIX `opendir` functionality.
*   **Parameters**: `dirname` (const char *) - The path of the directory to open.
*   **Returns**: A `gp_system_dir` handle to the opened directory.

#### `gp_system_readdir`

*   **Description**: Reads the next entry from an opened directory. Mirrors UNIX `readdir` functionality.
*   **Parameters**: `d` (gp_system_dir) - The handle to the opened directory.
*   **Returns**: A `gp_system_dirent` structure representing the directory entry.

#### `gp_system_filename`

*   **Description**: Retrieves the filename from a directory entry.
*   **Parameters**: `de` (gp_system_dirent) - The directory entry structure.
*   **Returns**: A constant character pointer to the filename.

#### `gp_system_closedir`

*   **Description**: Closes an opened directory. Mirrors UNIX `closedir` functionality.
*   **Parameters**: `dir` (gp_system_dir) - The handle to the opened directory.
*   **Returns**: An integer indicating success or failure.

#### `gp_system_is_file`

*   **Description**: Checks if a given path refers to a file.
*   **Parameters**: `filename` (const char *) - The path to check.
*   **Returns**: An integer indicating whether the path is a file (1) or not (0).

#### `gp_system_is_dir`

*   **Description**: Checks if a given path refers to a directory.
*   **Parameters**: `dirname` (const char *) - The path to check.
*   **Returns**: An integer indicating whether the path is a directory (1) or not (0).

```

### Create CameraFile from File Descriptor (C)

Initializes a new CameraFile object using an existing UNIX file descriptor. This function is useful for reading file data directly from a file descriptor. It populates a CameraFile structure pointed to by `_file_` and requires a valid file descriptor `_fd_` as input.

```c
int gp_file_new_from_fd(CameraFile **_file_, int _fd_)
```

--------------------------------

### Get Camera Storage Information (C)

Retrieves storage information (e.g., maximum and free space) for the camera's filesystem. This function requires a `CameraFilesystem` object, pointers to store `CameraStorageInformation` and the number of entries, and a `GPContext`. The storage information is returned in a newly allocated array, which the caller must free. Returns a gphoto2 error code, with `GP_ERROR_NOT_SUPPORTED` if the device does not support this feature.

```c
int gp_filesystem_get_storageinfo(
    CameraFilesystem * _fs_,
    CameraStorageInformation ** _storageinfo_,
    int * _nrofstorageinfos_,
    GPContext * _context_
);
```

--------------------------------

### Get Name of CameraList Entry in C

Retrieves the name of an entry at a specific index within a CameraList. This function is used when iterating through the list or accessing entries by their position. It requires the CameraList pointer, the index of the entry, and a pointer to store the retrieved name.

```c
int gp_list_get_name(CameraList *list, int index, const char **name)
```

--------------------------------

### C Camera Initialization Function Definition

Defines the function pointer type for camera initialization. This function is responsible for setting up the camera connection and requires a Camera object and GPContext for operation. It is a core component for camera library implementations.

```c
#ifndef __GPHOTO2_LIBRARY_H__
#define __GPHOTO2_LIBRARY_H__

#include <gphoto2/gphoto2-abilities-list.h>
#include <gphoto2/gphoto2-camera.h>

#ifdef __cplusplus
extern "C" {
#endif /* __cplusplus */

typedef int (* CameraLibraryIdFunc) (CameraText *id);

typedef int (* CameraLibraryAbilitiesFunc) (CameraAbilitiesList *list);

typedef int (* CameraLibraryInitFunc) (Camera *camera, GPContext *context);

/*
 * If you want to write a camera library, you need to implement 
 * the following three functions. Everything else should be declared
 * as static.
 */
int camera_id (CameraText *id);
int camera_abilities (CameraAbilitiesList *list);
int camera_init (Camera *camera, GPContext *context);

#ifdef __cplusplus
}
#endif /* __cplusplus */

#endif /* __GPHOTO2_LIBRARY_H__ */

```

--------------------------------

### Get Port Path - C

Retrieves the path associated with a specific port entry. This function is part of the libgphoto2 port information management system. It takes a GPPortInfo structure and a character pointer to store the path. The path typically represents the connection details for the port, like 'usb:001,023'.

```c
int gp_port_info_get_path(GPPortInfo info, char **path)
```

--------------------------------

### Get File Index by Name in gphoto2 Filesystem

Retrieves the index number of a file given its name within a specified folder on the camera's filesystem. This is the inverse operation of `gp_filesystem_name`. Requires a CameraFilesystem object, folder path, filename, and a GPContext. Returns a gphoto2 error code.

```c
int gp_filesystem_number(
    CameraFilesystem *  _fs_,
    const char *  _folder_,
    const char *  _filename_,
    GPContext *  _context_
);
```

--------------------------------

### Verify Device Permissions on FreeBSD (Newer Versions)

This command lists the details of devices within the `/dev/usb/` directory, showing their permissions, owner, group, and timestamps. On FreeBSD 8 and later, USB devices are organized under `/dev/usb/`. The output confirms the applied permissions and device structure.

```shell
ls -l /dev/usb/
```

--------------------------------

### Get Camera Storage Information (C)

Fetches storage information, such as maximum and free space, for a camera's filesystem. This function populates a provided array of CameraStorageInformation objects and the number of entries. The caller is responsible for freeing the allocated memory for the storage information. It returns a gphoto2 error code, with GP_ERROR_NOT_SUPPORTED being a possible error.

```c
int gp_filesystem_get_storageinfo(
    CameraFilesystem *  _fs_,
    CameraStorageInformation **  _storageinfo_,
    int *  _nrofstorageinfos_,
    GPContext *  _context_
);

### C: Create and Free GPPortInfo

Demonstrates the creation and deallocation of a GPPortInfo structure. This structure holds all the details about a specific camera port. Proper creation and freeing are crucial for memory management when working with individual port data.

```c
#include <gphoto2/gphoto2-port-info.h>

int main() {
    GPPortInfo info;
    int ret;

    // Create a new GPPortInfo structure
    ret = gp_port_info_new(&info);
    if (ret < 0) {
        // Handle error
        return ret;
    }

    // ... set or get port information using info ...

    // Free the GPPortInfo structure
    // Note: The function to free might be gp_port_info_free(info)
    // Check the actual library documentation for the correct function.
    // Assuming gp_port_info_free exists:
    // ret = gp_port_info_free(info);
    // if (ret < 0) {
    //     // Handle error
    // }

    return 0;
}
```

--------------------------------

### Get CameraWidget Child by Label, ID, or Name

Provides methods to find a child widget within a parent using different identifiers. `gp_widget_get_child_by_label`, `gp_widget_get_child_by_id`, and `gp_widget_get_child_by_name` allow searching for children by their visible label, unique ID, or internal name, respectively.

```c
int gp_widget_get_child_by_label (CameraWidget *widget, const char *label, CameraWidget **child)

### C: Create and Manage CameraList

Demonstrates the typical usage pattern for creating, populating, iterating, and freeing a CameraList object in C. This involves using functions like gp_list_new, gp_list_append, gp_list_count, gp_list_get_name, gp_list_get_value, and gp_list_free.

```c
CameraList *list;

gp_list_new(&list);

// Example: init_list_somehow(list); could involve gp_list_append or other population methods

// Iterate through the list
for (int i = 0; i < gp_list_count(list); i++) {
    const char *name;
    const char *value;
    gp_list_get_name(list, i, &name);
    gp_list_get_value(list, i, &value);
    // do_something_with(name, value);
}

gp_list_free(list);
```

gvfs-mount -l

### Configure usbcam.usermap for Hotplugging Cameras

This command redirects the output of `print-usb-usermap` to a hotplug configuration file. This step tells the hotplug system how to identify and handle USB cameras supported by libgphoto2. The target file may be `/etc/hotplug/usb/usbcam.usermap` or `/etc/hotplug/usb.usermap` depending on the distribution.

```bash
host:~# /usr/lib/libgphoto2/print-usb-usermap > /etc/hotplug/usb/usbcam.usermap
```

```bash
host:~# /usr/lib/libgphoto2/print-usb-usermap >> /etc/hotplug/usb.usermap
```

### Context Management API

Functions for creating, managing, and interacting with the gphoto2 context, which handles callbacks for user feedback, errors, and progress.

```APIDOC
## GPContext Operations

### Description
Provides functions to create, manage, and set callback functions for the GPContext, which is used for handling user interaction, errors, and progress reporting during camera operations.

### Method
Various (primarily C functions)

### Endpoint
N/A (C Library API)

### Parameters
#### Path Parameters
None

#### Query Parameters
None

#### Request Body
None

### Request Example
```c
GPContext *context = gp_context_new();
if (!context) { /* Handle error */ }

// Set callback functions
gp_context_set_error_func(context, my_error_handler, NULL);
gp_context_set_status_func(context, my_status_handler, NULL);
gp_context_set_question_func(context, my_question_handler, NULL);
gp_context_set_idle_func(context, my_idle_handler, NULL);
gp_context_set_message_func(context, my_message_handler, NULL);
gp_context_set_cancel_func(context, my_cancel_handler, NULL);

// Example of using progress functions
GPContextProgressStartFunc start_func = ...;
GPContextProgressUpdateFunc update_func = ...;
GPContextProgressStopFunc stop_func = ...;
gp_context_set_progress_funcs(context, start_func, update_func, stop_func, NULL);

// ... camera operations using the context ...

gp_context_unref(context); // Decrement reference count when done
```

### Response
#### Success Response (200)
N/A (C Library API, operations return status codes or modify state)

#### Response Example
N/A

## Functions

### `gp_context_new`

- **Description**: Creates a new context.
- **Return Value**: Pointer to a new `GPContext` object or NULL on failure.

### `gp_context_ref`

- **Description**: Increments the reference count of a context.
- **Parameters**:
  - `context` (*GPContext* *) - Pointer to the `GPContext` to reference.

### `gp_context_unref`

- **Description**: Decrements reference count of a context.
- **Parameters**:
  - `context` (*GPContext* *) - Pointer to the `GPContext` to unreference.

### `gp_context_set_idle_func`

- **Description**: Sets the idle function callback.
- **Parameters**:
  - `context` (*GPContext* *) - Pointer to the `GPContext`.
  - `func` (*GPContextIdleFunc*) - The callback function to set.
  - `data` (*void* *) - User data to pass to the callback.

### `gp_context_set_progress_funcs`

- **Description**: Sets the progress handling callback functions.
- **Parameters**:
  - `context` (*GPContext* *) - Pointer to the `GPContext`.
  - `start_func` (*GPContextProgressStartFunc*) - Callback for starting progress tracking.
  - `update_func` (*GPContextProgressUpdateFunc*) - Callback for updating progress.
  - `stop_func` (*GPContextProgressStopFunc*) - Callback for stopping progress tracking.
  - `data` (*void* *) - User data to pass to the callbacks.

### `gp_context_set_error_func`

- **Description**: Sets the error function callback.
- **Parameters**:
  - `context` (*GPContext* *) - Pointer to the `GPContext`.
  - `func` (*GPContextErrorFunc*) - The callback function to set.
  - `data` (*void* *) - User data to pass to the callback.

### `gp_context_set_status_func`

- **Description**: Sets the status function callback.
- **Parameters**:
  - `context` (*GPContext* *) - Pointer to the `GPContext`.
  - `func` (*GPContextStatusFunc*) - The callback function to set.
  - `data` (*void* *) - User data to pass to the callback.

### `gp_context_set_question_func`

- **Description**: Sets the question function callback.
- **Parameters**:
  - `context` (*GPContext* *) - Pointer to the `GPContext`.
  - `func` (*GPContextQuestionFunc*) - The callback function to set.
  - `data` (*void* *) - User data to pass to the callback.

### `gp_context_set_cancel_func`

- **Description**: Sets the cancel function callback.
- **Parameters**:
  - `context` (*GPContext* *) - Pointer to the `GPContext`.
  - `func` (*GPContextCancelFunc*) - The callback function to set.
  - `data` (*void* *) - User data to pass to the callback.

### `gp_context_set_message_func`

- **Description**: Sets the message function callback.
- **Parameters**:
  - `context` (*GPContext* *) - Pointer to the `GPContext`.
  - `func` (*GPContextMessageFunc*) - The callback function to set.
  - `data` (*void* *) - User data to pass to the callback.

### `gp_context_idle`

- **Description**: Notifies the frontend of a brief idle time.
- **Parameters**:
  - `context` (*GPContext* *) - Pointer to the `GPContext`.

### `gp_context_error`

- **Description**: Reports an error message through the context's error function.
- **Parameters**:
  - `context` (*GPContext* *) - Pointer to the `GPContext`.
  - `format` (*const char* *) - Format string for the error message.
  - `...` - Variable arguments for the format string.

### `gp_context_status`

- **Description**: Reports a status message through the context's status function.
- **Parameters**:
  - `context` (*GPContext* *) - Pointer to the `GPContext`.
  - `format` (*const char* *) - Format string for the status message.
  - `...` - Variable arguments for the format string.

### `gp_context_message`

- **Description**: Prints a message to the context's message handler.
- **Parameters**:
  - `context` (*GPContext* *) - Pointer to the `GPContext`.
  - `format` (*const char* *) - Format string for the message.
  - `...` - Variable arguments for the format string.

### `gp_context_question`

- **Description**: Asks the frontend user a question through the context's question function.
- **Parameters**:
  - `context` (*GPContext* *) - Pointer to the `GPContext`.
  - `format` (*const char* *) - Format string for the question.
  - `...` - Variable arguments for the format string.
- **Return Value**: `GPContextFeedback` indicating the user's response (e.g., OK, CANCEL).

### `gp_context_cancel`

- **Description**: Initiates a cancellation through the context's cancel function.
- **Parameters**:
  - `context` (*GPContext* *) - Pointer to the `GPContext`.
- **Return Value**: `GPContextFeedback` indicating the cancellation status.

### `gp_context_progress_start`

- **Description**: Starts progress tracking.
- **Parameters**:
  - `context` (*GPContext* *) - Pointer to the `GPContext`.
  - `target` (*float*) - The target value for the progress.
  - `format` (*const char* *) - Format string for the progress description.
  - `...` - Variable arguments for the format string.
- **Return Value**: An unsigned integer ID for the progress operation.

### `gp_context_progress_update`

- **Description**: Updates the current progress of an operation.
- **Parameters**:
  - `context` (*GPContext* *) - Pointer to the `GPContext`.
  - `id` (*unsigned int*) - The ID of the progress operation.
  - `current` (*float*) - The current progress value.

### `gp_context_progress_stop`

- **Description**: Stops progress tracking for an operation.
- **Parameters**:
  - `context` (*GPContext* *) - Pointer to the `GPContext`.
  - `id` (*unsigned int*) - The ID of the progress operation to stop.

```

### Configure Serial Port Settings in C

This C code snippet demonstrates how to configure settings for a serial port, including data bits, parity, stop bits, speed, and port name. It utilizes the `gphoto2-port.h` header.

```c
#include <gphoto2-port.h>

// Example usage of _GPPortSettingsSerial struct
struct _GPPortSettingsSerial serial_settings;

// Setting the port name
strcpy(serial_settings.port, "/dev/ttyS0");

// Setting the baudrate
serial_settings.speed = 9600;

// Setting the number of data bits
serial_settings.bits = 8;

// Setting the parity (e.g., no parity)
serial_settings.parity = GP_PORT_SERIAL_PARITY_NONE;

// Setting the number of stop bits
serial_settings.stopbits = 1;

// This struct would then be used with functions like gp_port_set_info()
```

```c

### Troubleshoot Linux 2.4.x USB Errors in libgphoto2

This FAQ entry acknowledges persistent issues with USB functionality on Linux 2.4.x, characterized by 'kernel: usb_control/bulk_msg: timeout' and 'kernel: usbdevfs: USBDEVFS_BULK failed' errors. It indicates that a known solution is not available and solicits user input.

```text
kernel: usb_control/bulk_msg: timeout
kernel: usbdevfs: USBDEVFS_BULK failed dev 3 ep 0x81 len 64 ret -110
    
```

### Camera Widget API Reference

Details on CameraWidget structure, types, and associated callbacks.

```APIDOC
## Camera Widget API Reference

### Description
Provides definitions for camera widget structures, types, and callback function signatures used in the libgphoto2 library.

### Data Structures

#### `CameraWidget`

- **Description**: Internal structure for camera widgets. Use accessor functions for interaction.

#### `CameraWidgetCallback`

- **Description**: Callback handler type for Button widgets. It takes a `Camera *`, `CameraWidget *`, and `GPContext *` as arguments.

### Enumerations

#### `CameraWidgetType`

- **Description**: Defines the types of widgets that can be created.

- **Values**:
  - `GP_WIDGET_WINDOW`: Represents a window widget.
  - `GP_WIDGET_SECTION`: Represents a section widget.
  - `GP_WIDGET_TEXT`: Represents a text input widget.
  - `GP_WIDGET_RANGE`: Represents a range slider widget.
  - `GP_WIDGET_TOGGLE`: Represents a toggle switch widget.
  - `GP_WIDGET_RADIO`: Represents a radio button widget.
  - `GP_WIDGET_MENU`: Represents a dropdown menu widget.
  - `GP_WIDGET_BUTTON`: Represents a button widget.
  - `GP_WIDGET_DATE`: Represents a date picker widget.

### Header Files

- `#include <gphoto2/gphoto2-widget.h>`

### Usage Notes

- Direct manipulation of the `CameraWidget` internal structure is discouraged; use provided accessor functions instead.
```

### Get and Set CameraFile MIME Type (C)

Functions for retrieving and setting the MIME type of a CameraFile. `gp_file_get_mime_type` obtains the current MIME type, while `gp_file_set_mime_type` allows explicit setting. `gp_file_detect_mime_type` attempts to automatically determine the MIME type based on the file's content or name.

```c
int gp_file_get_mime_type(CameraFile *file, const char **mime_type);
int gp_file_set_mime_type(CameraFile *file, const char *mime_type);
int gp_file_detect_mime_type(CameraFile *file);
```

### Check Serial Port Device File Permissions

Shows how to inspect the current permissions of a serial port device file (e.g., /dev/ttyS0) using the `ls -l` command. This helps understand who currently has access to the port.

```bash
host:~# **ls -l /dev/ttyS0**
crw-rw----    1 root     dialout    4,  64 Jul  5 12:05 /dev/ttyS0
host:~# 
	
```

### gphoto2.h Header - Core Definitions

The main header file for the libgphoto2 library. It includes definitions for C++ linkage and includes other essential port and library-specific headers like gphoto2-port.h, gphoto2-file.h, and gphoto2-library.h. It also contains conditional includes for OS2 and WIN32 environments.

```c
#ifndef __GPHOTO2_H__
#define __GPHOTO2_H__

#ifdef __cplusplus
extern "C" {
#endif

#ifdef OS2
# include <db.h>
# include <sys/param.h>
# define CAMLIBS getenv("CAMLIBS")
# define RTLD_LAZY 0x001
# define VERSION "2"
# define usleep(t) _sleep2(((t)+500)/ 1000)
#endif

#ifdef WIN32
#undef CAMLIBS
#define CAMLIBS "."
#endif

#include <gphoto2/gphoto2-port.h>
#include <gphoto2/gphoto2-port-log.h>
#include <gphoto2/gphoto2-port-result.h>

#include <gphoto2/gphoto2-file.h>
#include <gphoto2/gphoto2-library.h>
#include <gphoto2/gphoto2-setting.h>

#ifdef __cplusplus
}
#endif

#endif /* __GPHOTO2_H__ */

```

### Manage Camera Folders

Functions for interacting with the camera's file system, including listing files and folders, deleting all files, creating directories, and removing directories.

```c
int gp_camera_folder_list_files (Camera *camera, const char *folder, CameraList *list, GPContext *context)
int gp_camera_folder_list_folders (Camera *camera, const char *folder, CameraList *list, GPContext *context)

### C: libgphoto2 Port Settings and Operations

Defines structures and function prototypes for configuring and operating camera ports within the libgphoto2 library. This includes serial and USB port settings, as well as functions for opening, closing, reading, writing, and controlling port states. It also covers USB-specific operations like finding devices and sending control messages.

```c
#ifndef __GPHOTO2_PORT_H__
#define __GPHOTO2_PORT_H__

#include <gphoto2/gphoto2-port-info-list.h>

/* For portability */
#include <gphoto2/gphoto2-port-portability.h>
#ifdef OS2
#include <gphoto2/gphoto2-port-portability-os2.h>
#include <os2.h>
#endif

#ifdef __cplusplus
extern "C" {
#endif /* __cplusplus */

#ifndef TRUE
#define TRUE (0==0)
#endif

#ifndef FALSE
#define FALSE (1==0)
#endif

typedef enum _GPPortSerialParity
{
GP_PORT_SERIAL_PARITY_OFF = 0,
GP_PORT_SERIAL_PARITY_EVEN,
GP_PORT_SERIAL_PARITY_ODD
} GPPortSerialParity;

#define GP_PORT_MAX_BUF_LEN 4096 

typedef struct _GPPortSettingsSerial {
char port[128]; 
int speed; 
int bits; 
GPPortSerialParity parity; 
int stopbits; 
} GPPortSettingsSerial;

typedef struct _GPPortSettingsUSB {
int inep; 
int outep; 
int intep; 
int config; 
int interface; 
int altsetting; 
int maxpacketsize; 
/* must be last to avoid binary incompatibility.
 * luckily we just need to make sure this struct does not 
 * get larger than _GPPortSettingsSerial. */
char port[64]; 
} GPPortSettingsUSB;

typedef struct _GPPortSettingsUsbDiskDirect {
char path[128]; 
} GPPortSettingsUsbDiskDirect;

typedef struct _GPPortSettingsUsbScsi {
char path[128]; 
} GPPortSettingsUsbScsi;

typedef union _GPPortSettings {
GPPortSettingsSerial serial; 
GPPortSettingsUSB usb; 
GPPortSettingsUsbDiskDirect usbdiskdirect; 
GPPortSettingsUsbScsi usbscsi; 
} GPPortSettings;

enum {
GP_PORT_USB_ENDPOINT_IN,
GP_PORT_USB_ENDPOINT_OUT,
GP_PORT_USB_ENDPOINT_INT
};

typedef struct _GPPortPrivateLibrary GPPortPrivateLibrary;
typedef struct _GPPortPrivateCore GPPortPrivateCore;

typedef struct _GPPort {
/* For your convenience */
GPPortType type; 
GPPortSettings settings; 
GPPortSettings settings_pending;
int timeout; 
GPPortPrivateLibrary *pl; 
GPPortPrivateCore *pc; 
} GPPort;

int gp_port_new (GPPort **port);
int gp_port_free (GPPort *port);

int gp_port_set_info (GPPort *port, GPPortInfo info);
int gp_port_get_info (GPPort *port, GPPortInfo *info);

int gp_port_open (GPPort *port);
int gp_port_close (GPPort *port);

int gp_port_reset (GPPort *port);

int gp_port_write (GPPort *port, const char *data, int size);
int gp_port_read (GPPort *port, char *data, int size);
int gp_port_check_int (GPPort *port, char *data, int size);
int gp_port_check_int_fast (GPPort *port, char *data, int size);

int gp_port_get_timeout (GPPort *port, int *timeout);
int gp_port_set_timeout (GPPort *port, int timeout);

int gp_port_set_settings (GPPort *port, GPPortSettings settings);
int gp_port_get_settings (GPPort *port, GPPortSettings *settings);

typedef enum _GPPin {
GP_PIN_RTS,
GP_PIN_DTR,
GP_PIN_CTS,
GP_PIN_DSR,
GP_PIN_CD,
GP_PIN_RING
} GPPin;

typedef enum _GPLevel {
GP_LEVEL_LOW = 0,
GP_LEVEL_HIGH = 1 
} GPLevel;

int gp_port_get_pin (GPPort *port, GPPin pin, GPLevel *level);
int gp_port_set_pin (GPPort *port, GPPin pin, GPLevel level);

int gp_port_send_break (GPPort *port, int duration);
int gp_port_flush (GPPort *port, int direction);

int gp_port_usb_find_device (GPPort *port, int idvendor, int idproduct);
int gp_port_usb_find_device_by_class (GPPort *port, int mainclass, int subclass, int protocol);
int gp_port_usb_clear_halt (GPPort *port, int ep);
int gp_port_usb_msg_write (GPPort *port, int request, int value,
int index, char *bytes, int size);
int gp_port_usb_msg_read (GPPort *port, int request, int value,
int index, char *bytes, int size);
int gp_port_usb_msg_interface_write (GPPort *port, int request, 
int value, int index, char *bytes, int size);
int gp_port_usb_msg_interface_read (GPPort *port, int request, 
int value, int index, char *bytes, int size);
int gp_port_usb_msg_class_write (GPPort *port, int request, 
int value, int index, char *bytes, int size);

#endif

```

### Wait Event Functionality

Details on how to use the wait-event option for timed operations and event monitoring.

```APIDOC
## Wait Event Functionality

### Description
Details on how to use the wait-event option for timed operations and event monitoring.

### `--wait-event[=<VALUE>]`

#### Description
Waits for a specified event or duration. The value can be in seconds (s), milliseconds (ms), number of events, or a substring. Defaults to 1 second if no value is provided.

#### Parameters
#### Path Parameters
* None

#### Query Parameters
* `VALUE` (string/number) - Optional. Specifies the duration or event criteria. Examples: `5s`, `500ms`, `5` (events), or a substring.

#### Request Body
* None

#### Example
```bash
# Wait for 5 seconds
gphoto2 --wait-event=5s

# Wait for 500 milliseconds
gphoto2 --wait-event=500ms

# Wait for 5 events
gphoto2 --wait-event=5

# Wait for an event matching a substring (driver dependent)
gphoto2 --wait-event=camera_connected
```

#### Response
#### Success Response (0)
* Exit code 0 indicates successful completion or timeout reached.

#### Response Example
(No direct response body, completion indicated by exit code and subsequent commands/scripts)

#### Error Handling
* Timeout: If no event occurs within the specified duration, the command exits successfully after the timeout.
* Driver Support: Requires camera driver support for event monitoring.
```

### GPContext Structure and Typedefs

Documentation for the GPContext structure and related enumerations used for callback handling and feedback mechanisms.

```APIDOC
## Typedef Documentation

typedef struct _GPContext GPContext
---

The gphoto context structure.
This structure allows callback handling, passing error contexts back, progress handling and download cancellation and similar things. It is usually passed around the functions.

typedef enum _GPContextFeedback GPContextFeedback
---

Return codes that can be returned by progress handling.
An application can return special values back to the libgphoto2 progress callback handling functions. If "Cancel" is selected, libgphoto2 and the camera driver will try to cancel transfer.

## Enumeration Type Documentation

enum _GPContextFeedback
---

Return codes that can be returned by progress handling.
An application can return special values back to the libgphoto2 progress callback handling functions. If "Cancel" is selected, libgphoto2 and the camera driver will try to cancel transfer.

Enumerator
---

GP_CONTEXT_FEEDBACK_OK | Everything ok... proceed.
GP_CONTEXT_FEEDBACK_CANCEL | Please cancel the current transfer if possible.
```

### GPPortInfo Structure Members

Describes the members of the _GPPortInfo structure in C. Each member's type, name, and a brief description of its purpose are provided, along with its definition location within the header file.

```c
char * name
The name of this port (usb:)
**Definition:** gphoto2-port-info.h:34
```

```c
char * path
The path of this port (usb:001,023)
**Definition:** gphoto2-port-info.h:35
```

```c
char * library_filename
Internal pathname of the port driver. Do not use outside of the port library.
**Definition:** gphoto2-port-info.h:38
```

```c
GPPortType type
The type of this port.
**Definition:** gphoto2-port-info.h:33

### Create CameraFile Objects (C)

int gp_file_new(CameraFile **file);
int gp_file_new_from_fd(CameraFile **file, int fd);
int gp_file_new_from_handler(CameraFile **file, CameraFileHandler *handler, void *priv);

### Load Camera Drivers into Abilities List (C)

Scans the system for camera drivers and adds all supported camera models to the provided CameraAbilitiesList. This function utilizes gp_abilities_list_count() and gp_port_usb_find_device() related functions, referencing GP_ERROR_IO_USB_FIND and GP_OK.

```c
int gp_abilities_list_load(
    CameraAbilitiesList *_list_,
    GPContext *_context_
);
```

--------------------------------

### FreeBSD devfs.rules for USB Camera Permissions (8 and over)

This configuration snippet is for FreeBSD versions 8 and newer. It defines rules for the devfs framework to manage permissions for dynamically created USB devices, enabling non-root users to access USB cameras and mass storage devices. It grants read/write access to the 'usb' group for specified device paths.

```bash
[usb_devices=10]
add path 'usb/*' mode 0660 group usb
add path 'da*s*' mode 0660 group usb
```

int gp_file_new_from_fd (CameraFile ** _file_ , int _fd_ )
```

### File Management Functions

Functions for creating, manipulating, and managing camera files within the libgphoto2 library.

```APIDOC
## File Management Functions

### Description
Provides functions for creating, initializing, referencing, freeing, and setting properties of `CameraFile` objects.

### Functions

- **`gp_file_new`**
  - **Description**: Creates a new `CameraFile` object.
  - **Parameters**:
    - `file` (CameraFile **): Pointer to a `CameraFile` pointer to store the newly created object.
  - **Returns**: `int` - 0 on success, negative on error.

- **`gp_file_new_from_fd`**
  - **Description**: Creates a new `CameraFile` object from a file descriptor.
  - **Parameters**:
    - `file` (CameraFile **): Pointer to a `CameraFile` pointer.
    - `fd` (int): The file descriptor.
  - **Returns**: `int` - 0 on success, negative on error.

- **`gp_file_new_from_handler`**
  - **Description**: Creates a new `CameraFile` object using a custom file handler.
  - **Parameters**:
    - `file` (CameraFile **): Pointer to a `CameraFile` pointer.
    - `handler` (CameraFileHandler *): The custom file handler.
    - `priv` (void *): Private data for the handler.
  - **Returns**: `int` - 0 on success, negative on error.

- **`gp_file_ref`**
  - **Description**: Increases the reference counter for a `CameraFile` object.
  - **Parameters**:
    - `file` (CameraFile *): Pointer to the `CameraFile` object.
  - **Returns**: `int` - 0 on success, negative on error.

- **`gp_file_unref`**
  - **Description**: Decreases the reference counter for a `CameraFile` object.
  - **Parameters**:
    - `file` (CameraFile *): Pointer to the `CameraFile` object.
  - **Returns**: `int` - 0 on success, negative on error.

- **`gp_file_free`**
  - **Description**: Destroys a `CameraFile` object.
  - **Parameters**:
    - `file` (CameraFile *): Pointer to the `CameraFile` object.
  - **Returns**: `int` - 0 on success, negative on error.

- **`gp_file_set_name`**
  - **Description**: Sets the name of the `CameraFile`.
  - **Parameters**:
    - `file` (CameraFile *): Pointer to the `CameraFile` object.
    - `name` (const char *): The desired name for the file.
  - **Returns**: `int` - 0 on success, negative on error.

- **`gp_file_get_name`**
  - **Description**: Retrieves the name of the `CameraFile`.
  - **Parameters**:
    - `file` (CameraFile *): Pointer to the `CameraFile` object.
    - `name` (const char **): Pointer to a character pointer where the name will be stored.
  - **Returns**: `int` - 0 on success, negative on error.

- **`gp_file_set_mime_type`**
  - **Description**: Sets the MIME type of the `CameraFile`.
  - **Parameters**:
    - `file` (CameraFile *): Pointer to the `CameraFile` object.
    - `mime_type` (const char *): The MIME type string.
  - **Returns**: `int` - 0 on success, negative on error.

- **`gp_file_get_mime_type`**
  - **Description**: Retrieves the MIME type of the `CameraFile`.
  - **Parameters**:
    - `file` (CameraFile *): Pointer to the `CameraFile` object.
    - `mime_type` (const char **): Pointer to a character pointer where the MIME type will be stored.
  - **Returns**: `int` - 0 on success, negative on error.

- **`gp_file_set_mtime`**
  - **Description**: Sets the modification time of the `CameraFile`.
  - **Parameters**:
    - `file` (CameraFile *): Pointer to the `CameraFile` object.
    - `mtime` (time_t): The modification time (seconds since Epoch).
  - **Returns**: `int` - 0 on success, negative on error.

- **`gp_file_get_mtime`**
  - **Description**: Retrieves the modification time of the `CameraFile`.
  - **Parameters**:
    - `file` (CameraFile *): Pointer to the `CameraFile` object.
    - `mtime` (time_t *): Pointer to a `time_t` where the modification time will be stored.
  - **Returns**: `int` - 0 on success, negative on error.

- **`gp_file_detect_mime_type`**
  - **Description**: Automatically detects the MIME type of the `CameraFile` based on its content or name.
  - **Parameters**:
    - `file` (CameraFile *): Pointer to the `CameraFile` object.
  - **Returns**: `int` - 0 on success, negative on error.

- **`gp_file_adjust_name_for_mime_type`**
  - **Description**: Adjusts the filename to be appropriate for its detected MIME type.
  - **Parameters**:
    - `file` (CameraFile *): Pointer to the `CameraFile` object.
  - **Returns**: `int` - 0 on success, negative on error.

- **`gp_file_get_name_by_type`**
  - **Description**: Generates a filename suitable for a specific file type.
  - **Parameters**:
    - `file` (CameraFile *): Pointer to the `CameraFile` object.
    - `basename` (const char *): The base name for the file.
    - `type` (CameraFileType): The type of file (e.g., preview, raw).
    - `newname` (char **): Pointer to a character pointer where the generated filename will be stored.
  - **Returns**: `int` - 0 on success, negative on error.

- **`gp_file_set_data_and_size`**
  - **Description**: Sets the data and size of the `CameraFile`.
  - **Parameters**:
    - `file` (CameraFile *): Pointer to the `CameraFile` object.
    - `data` (char *): Pointer to the file data.
    - `size` (unsigned long int): The size of the data in bytes.
  - **Returns**: `int` - 0 on success, negative on error.

- **`gp_file_get_data_and_size`**
  - **Description**: Retrieves the data and size of the `CameraFile`.
  - **Parameters**:
    - `file` (CameraFile *): Pointer to the `CameraFile` object.
    - `data` (const char **): Pointer to a character pointer where the data pointer will be stored.
    - `size` (unsigned long int *): Pointer to an unsigned long int where the size will be stored.
  - **Returns**: `int` - 0 on success, negative on error.

- **`gp_file_open`**
  - **Description**: Opens a file for the `CameraFile` object.
  - **Parameters**:
    - `file` (CameraFile *): Pointer to the `CameraFile` object.
    - `filename` (const char *): The name of the file to open.
  - **Returns**: `int` - 0 on success, negative on error.

- **`gp_file_save`**
  - **Description**: Saves the content of the `CameraFile` to a specified filename.
  - **Parameters**:
    - `file` (CameraFile *): Pointer to the `CameraFile` object.
    - `filename` (const char *): The name of the file to save to.
  - **Returns**: `int` - 0 on success, negative on error.

- **`gp_file_clean`**
  - **Description**: Cleans the content of the `CameraFile` object.
  - **Parameters**:
    - `file` (CameraFile *): Pointer to the `CameraFile` object.
  - **Returns**: `int` - 0 on success, negative on error.

- **`gp_file_copy`**
  - **Description**: Copies the content from a source `CameraFile` to a destination `CameraFile`.
  - **Parameters**:
    - `destination` (CameraFile *): Pointer to the destination `CameraFile`.
    - `source` (CameraFile *): Pointer to the source `CameraFile`.
  - **Returns**: `int` - 0 on success, negative on error.

- **`gp_file_append`**
  - **Description**: Appends data to the `CameraFile`.
  - **Parameters**:
    - `file` (CameraFile *): Pointer to the `CameraFile` object.
    - `data` (const char *): Pointer to the data to append.
    - `size` (unsigned long int): The size of the data to append.
  - **Returns**: `int` - 0 on success, negative on error.

- **`gp_file_slurp`**
  - **Description**: Reads data from the `CameraFile` into a buffer.
  - **Parameters**:
    - `file` (CameraFile *): Pointer to the `CameraFile` object.
    - `data` (char *): Pointer to the buffer to store the data.
    - `size` (size_t): The maximum size of the buffer.
    - `readlen` (size_t *): Pointer to a `size_t` where the number of bytes read will be stored.
  - **Returns**: `int` - 0 on success, negative on error.

```

### GPVersionVerbosity Enumeration (C)

Defines verbosity levels for version information retrieval in libgphoto2. GP_VERSION_SHORT provides a concise version string, while GP_VERSION_VERBOSE offers a more detailed output. This enumeration is relevant for functions like gp_port_library_version.

```c
enum GPVersionVerbosity {
  GP_VERSION_SHORT = 0,
  GP_VERSION_VERBOSE = 1
}
```

--------------------------------

### Port Operations and Settings (C)

Defines structures and types for handling camera port operations and settings. This includes GPPort, GPPortOperations, GPPortSettings, and specific settings for serial and USB connections. It also defines logging levels and callback functions.

```c
/* Port and Logging Definitions */
typedef struct _GPPort GPPort;
typedef struct _GPPortOperations GPPortOperations;
typedef struct _GPPortSettings GPPortSettings;
typedef struct {
    int dummy;
} GPPortSettingsSerial;
typedef struct {
    int dummy;
} GPPortSettingsUSB;
typedef struct {
    int dummy;
} GPPortSettingsUsbDiskDirect;
typedef struct {
    int dummy;
} GPPortSettingsUsbScsi;
typedef enum {
    GPLevel_Off = 0,
    GPLevel_Error,
    GPLevel_Warnings,
    GPLevel_Information,
    GPLevel_Debug,
    GPLevel_All
} GPLogLevel;
typedef void (*GPLogFunc) (GPLogLevel level, const char *domain, const char *message, void *data);
typedef enum {
    GPPortType_Unknown = 0,
    GPPortType_Serial,
    GPPortType_USB,
    GPPortType_USBDisk,
    GPPortType_MTP,
    GPPortType_PTPIP
} GPPortType;
typedef enum {
    GPPortSerialParity_None,
    GPPortSerialParity_Odd,
    GPPortSerialParity_Even
} GPPortSerialParity;
typedef struct {
    int dummy;
} GPPin;
```

--------------------------------

### Folder Operations API

APIs for creating and removing directories on the camera.

```APIDOC
## POST /folder

### Description
Creates a new directory on the camera.

### Method
POST

### Endpoint
`/folder`

### Parameters
#### Query Parameters
- **fs** (CameraFilesystem*) - Required - Pointer to the CameraFilesystem structure.
- **folder** (const char*) - Required - The parent folder where the new directory will be created.
- **name** (const char*) - Required - The name of the new directory.
- **context** (GPContext*) - Required - Pointer to the GPContext for operation.

### Response
#### Success Response (200)
- **int** - Returns 0 on success, non-zero on error.

#### Response Example
```json
{
  "status": "success"
}
```

## DELETE /folder

### Description
Removes a directory from the camera.

### Method
DELETE

### Endpoint
`/folder`

### Parameters
#### Query Parameters
- **fs** (CameraFilesystem*) - Required - Pointer to the CameraFilesystem structure.
- **folder** (const char*) - Required - The path of the directory to remove.
- **name** (const char*) - Required - The name of the directory to remove.
- **context** (GPContext*) - Required - Pointer to the GPContext for operation.

### Response
#### Success Response (200)
- **int** - Returns 0 on success, non-zero on error.

#### Response Example
```json
{
  "status": "success"
}
```
```

--------------------------------

### libgphoto2 Camera File Data Handling (C)

Functions for setting and retrieving the raw data and size of a camera file. These are fundamental operations for loading or saving file content directly.

```c
int gp_file_set_data_and_size (CameraFile*, char *data,
 unsigned long int size);
int gp_file_get_data_and_size (CameraFile*, const char **data,
 unsigned long int *size);
```

--------------------------------

### Make USB Camera Hotplug Script Executable

This command sets the execute permission for the `/etc/hotplug/usb/usbcam` script. This is the final step in enabling the hotplug system to run the script when a USB camera is detected, allowing it to be properly recognized and accessed.

```bash
host:~# chmod +x /etc/hotplug/usb/usbcam
```

--------------------------------

### Camera Information and Abilities

Functions to retrieve information about the camera and its capabilities.

```APIDOC
## Camera Information and Abilities

### Description
Functions for retrieving general information and the supported abilities of the connected camera.

### Method
Library Functions

### Functions
- **camera_id()**: Retrieves a unique identifier for the camera.
- **camera_summary()**: Gets a summary of the camera's status and capabilities.
- **camera_abilities()**: Retrieves a list of the camera's supported abilities.

### Related Headers
- gphoto2-library.h
- gphoto2-library.c
- template.c
```

--------------------------------

### gp_filesystem_make_dir

Creates a new subfolder within a specified folder on the camera's filesystem.

```APIDOC
## gp_filesystem_make_dir

### Description
Create a subfolder within a folder.

### Method
N/A (C function)

### Endpoint
N/A (C function)

### Parameters
#### Path Parameters
None

#### Query Parameters
None

#### Request Body
None

### Request Example
N/A

### Response
#### Success Response (GP_OK)
Returns a gphoto2 error code indicating success.

#### Response Example
N/A

### Errors
- GP_ERROR_DIRECTORY_NOT_FOUND
- GP_ERROR_NOT_SUPPORTED
```
